Current Commentary

A Glimpse into the Inside Story of the German Coup 33

— Heng

There has been talk for weeks about a potential coup in Germany. Unexpectedly, before the coup could even be launched, Hitler swiftly suppressed it with lightning speed. The swiftness of his actions has been praised by many. However, whether those suppressed by Hitler were enemies or loyal followers of his own party remains questionable. This is because the main force behind the anticipated coup was believed to be the Reichswehr (German army). Yet, those actually punished by Hitler were the Sturmabteilung (SA), or Storm Troopers, which he himself created. Furthermore, according to German telegrams, the Reichswehr also mobilized to assist during the arrest of the SA leaders, raising the first point of suspicion. The Reichswehr, known for its right-wing leanings, assisted Hitler. Therefore, it seems unlikely that Kurt von Schleicher, a former Reichswehr leader, should have been killed by Hitler. However, the reality proves otherwise, raising the second point of suspicion. Vice-Chancellor Franz von Papen, a well-known restorationist and a confidant of Hindenburg, was also involved. If Hitler's actions were instigated by the right wing, then monitoring Papen seems pointless, raising the third point of suspicion. Moreover, according to German officialdom's declarations, aside from Hitler's anger at his followers' immorality, scandalous behavior, and extravagant lifestyle, the purpose of Hitler's actions remains unclear. In reality, since Hitler's rise to power, countless of his followers have become nominal members of large industrial and commercial enterprises, enjoying substantial salaries. Why would Hitler, who has always been tolerant, suddenly become strict today? This raises the fourth point of suspicion. With these four suspicions, we do not know whether Hitler's astonishing actions were truly to eradicate the left wing for the right wing, or to suppress the right wing for the left wing, or to genuinely eliminate corrupt elements within the party. Before the truth is fully revealed, we cannot make a definitive judgment. However, observing the developments after the rise of the National Socialist Party, Hitler's recent actions seem to symbolize the gradual rise of the right wing.

The National Socialist Party's past victories have all been aided by the middle class, small merchants, and small farmers. Therefore, when it rose, commentators all spoke of the rise of the middle class. However, facts from the past year and a half have proven that small merchants and small farmers have not received the special benefits promised by the Nazi Party's program. The small merchants hoped that the Nazi Party would implement its policies of closing department stores and supporting retailers. The small and poor farmers hoped for the confiscation of large estates and the abolition of usury. However, the Nazi Party only paid lip service and did not deliver. The reason for this breach of promise is that before the National Socialist Party came to power, it had already received funding from the financial community and large industrial enterprises. After taking power, general financial and industrial institutions, department stores, and large-scale cooperatives all successively appointed National Socialist Party members as committee members, giving them supervisory positions with very generous salaries. Jewish-owned stores were entirely managed by National Socialist Party members. Therefore, their interests not only did not conflict with those of the big capitalists, but were also intertwined. It is difficult to expect them to keep their pre-election promises. The failure to confiscate large estates and the failure to reduce interest rates on farmers' loans are similar problems.

However, this kind of change in life is still limited to the middle-level members of the National Socialist Party, while the changes among the upper-level members are even greater. Hitler's relationship with the major financier Hjalmar Schacht and the major steel industrialist Fritz Thyssen are the most prominent examples. Hitler's campaign funds for the several elections in 1932 largely came from these two individuals. This is the first reason for Hitler's right-wing leanings. Hitler's right-hand man, Hermann Göring, recently married the daughter of the German steel magnate Fritz Thyssen, further strengthening his relationship with industrialists. Göring's right-wing leanings have always been the most pronounced among the National Socialist Party leaders. Now that Hitler has eliminated dissidents, Göring is of paramount importance and extremely effective. This is the second reason for Hitler's right-wing leanings.

In summary, based on Hitler's actions over the years and his current actions, it seems that he has already leaned towards the embrace of the big capitalists. He fears a left-wing uprising, so he is carrying out a large-scale massacre with preemptive measures to rebuild his waning prestige and make his followers blindly follow him. However, whether the National Socialist Party members, after this stimulation, can remain eternally loyal to Hitler remains to be proven by facts. The exposure of the corrupt lives of National Socialist Party members has given the people a very bad impression. Whether they can still cherish the National Socialist Party's ideology is also uncertain.

The Climate in Suzhou is Cool

(Suzhou) At 5:45 PM today, a gale and rainstorm occurred at Hukou Pass on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Line, lasting for more than half an hour. Also, in Suzhou City at around 6:00 PM, there was a strong wind for an hour, followed by heavy rain for a few minutes. The climate is cool. The northern sky appeared scarlet red for half a day, then turned cyan, and then scarlet again after another five minutes, forming a spectacular sight. The current temperature is 89 degrees. (3rd Special Dispatch)

The Relaxation of Discipline and the Repeated Bribery Cases Forced the Saito Cabinet to Resign 55

In Office for Two Years and One Month

The Future of Political Power Awaits Saionji's Decision

(Tokyo) The cabinet convened at 10:25 AM this morning and unanimously resolved to resign en masse. Thus, the Saito Cabinet, which took office on May 22, 1932, came to an end. (3rd Reuters Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Minister of Justice Oyama visited Prime Minister Saito at 7:10 AM this morning to deliver the final report on the bribery case in the Ministry of Finance. Prime Minister Saito also summoned Minister of Railways Mitsuchi, Minister of Navy Osumi, and Minister of Commerce Matsumoto before the cabinet meeting at 10:25 AM to inform them of the decision to resign en masse and seek the understanding of the cabinet members. Minister of Finance Takahashi also arrived at the Prime Minister's residence at 9:40 AM. The cabinet meeting was held at 10:25 AM. Prime Minister Saito stood up and, with a somber expression, reported the bribery case in the Ministry of Finance and the bribery facts of former cabinet members, saying that the current cabinet must take responsibility and resign en masse. The atmosphere was extremely sad throughout the meeting. (3rd Hualian Electric)

Listening to the Report of the Minister of Justice 56

(Tokyo) After Prime Minister Saito met with Minister of Justice Oyama this morning and listened to his report on the Ministry of Finance incident, he attended the cabinet meeting at 10:20 AM. As a result of consulting with the members on the attitude the cabinet should take, it was decided to resign en masse. (3rd Nichiren Electric)

(Tokyo) Prime Minister Saito maintained a wait-and-see attitude for more than forty days since the Ministry of Finance incident was discovered. Today, after listening to the report from Minister of Justice Oyama and understanding all the facts, he decided to resign to take responsibility. He attended the cabinet meeting and said to the members that the purpose of the current cabinet's establishment was to rectify discipline. However, a discipline problem has occurred within this cabinet, which is intolerable. We should immediately take this responsibility and resign en masse. All cabinet members expressed their agreement with the Prime Minister's tragic decision. The Prime Minister then took the resignation letters of all members to the Imperial Palace. (3rd Nichiren Electric)

The Cabinet Submits Its Resignation En Masse 57

(Tokyo) At 11:50 AM this morning, the cabinet meeting had decided on the cabinet's resignation en masse. Prime Minister Saito immediately gathered the resignation letters of all cabinet members and entered the palace to meet with the Emperor. He presented the resignation letters with a letter of reasons, the general idea being that a discipline problem had occurred within the government departments, which had caused public sentiment to waver, and he was afraid. He immediately submitted his resignation and requested permission. The Emperor instructed that he should continue to oversee political affairs until there was an order. The Prime Minister withdrew and reopened the cabinet meeting to convey the imperial decree. The Emperor summoned Makino Naifu (Lord Keeper of the Privy Seal) to inquire. Makino Naifu replied that he should inquire of Prince Saionji. Thereupon, Vice-Chamberlain Hirohata was ordered in the afternoon to go to Gotemba to convey the Emperor's inquiry to Prince Saionji. If Prince Saionji replies immediately, then the trend of political power can be determined tomorrow (i.e., the 4th). If Prince Saionji comes to Tokyo, it may be delayed for two or three days. (3rd Dentsu Electric)

Moreover, because the cabinet was a puppet of political parties and drove out the fascists, the fascists cooperated with the court's prosecution bureau and decided to carry out the so-called legal May 15 Incident. Speculation on Successor Candidates 61

It is Hoped that Saito Makoto Will Rise Again and Form a Cabinet

The Theory That Yamamoto Will Succeed is Also Quite Strong

(Tokyo) Who will be the successor to the cabinet? This is the goal of the nation's attention. Combining information from all sides, it seems difficult for Governor-General Ugaki to be realized due to the strong opposition from the military. The theory of Privy Council President Ichiki forming a cabinet cannot be believed, because there is a major reason why Ichiki assumed the position of Privy Council President. The senior vassals are unwilling to easily change his position. As for the Kiyoura cabinet theory, because he is too old and his relationship with the military is not as close as it used to be, although there are various rumors in the world, his succession theory does not seem to be realized. From this point of view, the view that Saito Makoto will form a cabinet again can be said to be the most powerful. The second Saito cabinet will be organized with a restructuring policy, and it is also possible that the political parties will support its future. (3rd Nichiren Electric)

(Tokyo) To what kind of person will Prince Saionji奏請(奏請, formally request the emperor) regarding the selection of the leader of the succeeding cabinet? All aspects are paying close attention. However, Prince Saionji and Makino Naifu both seem to advocate that in order to deal with the situation, it is not appropriate to choose an unreasonable path. Before entering the palace on the 4th, it is said that they plan to discuss with Makino Naifu and other senior vassals before奉答(奉答, formally reply to the emperor) to the Emperor. From the fact that Prince Saionji will return to Gotemba on the same day and the circumstances of his surroundings, it is likely that he will still奏請(奏請) that the imperial command be降(降, bestow, as in the Emperor bestow an order) to Saito again, as a plan to quickly resolve the political situation. Reckoning of the Saito Cabinet's Two-Year Reign 65

Relying on the whims of the military clique, creating a puppet state, issuing large amounts of public debt, preparing for a future war

(Tokyo) After the May 15th Incident of 1932, in which members of the Japanese army, navy, and a suicide squad of farmers assassinated Prime Minister Inukai and plotted a fascist revolution, Japanese domestic politics were thrown into disarray. Viscount Saito, entrusted by elder statesmen and financial magnates, formed a cabinet on the 26th, bearing the following missions: (1) to suppress revolutionary movements from both the left and right wings; (2) to resolve the issue of military expansion and prepare for a major war; (3) to alleviate the poverty of farmers; and (4) to resolve the Manchurian policy. After assuming office, Prime Minister Saito devoted himself to resolving these four major issues. A brief account of the process is as follows: (1) In order to suppress domestic revolutionary movements, a special security force was established in the capital, wireless stations were set up in various prefectures, special agent teams were increased, remnants of the Communist Party were rounded up during emergencies, and the Godspeed Corps was captured to prevent the conspiracies of military cliques. Japanese nationals with military registration entering and leaving Manchuria were strictly investigated, even the wooden coffins of fallen Japanese soldiers were inspected. Fascists were expelled to Manchuria and China, with no effort spared. In May of this year, the president of the Privy Council was replaced, delivering a final blow to the fascists. This was the main effort to prevent revolution, providing Japanese financial groups with a prescription for prolonging their lives, but the results were not very effective. (2) After Saito came to power, the Second Naval Replenishment Plan was immediately decided, with an expenditure of 760 million yen. It was planned to build 24 warships over three years, and the air force was to be increased from 31 to 39 squadrons. The army decided to dispatch four more divisions to the four eastern provinces on a permanent basis, with half of the expenses borne by the puppet organization. The army also decided on a military supplies replenishment fee of 870,084,900 yen, to be fully replenished over five years. Thus, preliminary preparations for a major war were indeed ready. (3) The May 15th Incident was a coup d'état led by the military and involving farmers. Therefore, the cabinet and political parties had to find a way to resolve this problem. As a result, 700 million yen was spent over these three years to start projects in rural areas to help farmers. In reality, farmers benefited very little. Most of the funds went to financial capitalists and domestic manufacturers, and farmers remained poor. Araki, the Minister of the Army, who took it upon himself to save the farmers, also had to step down. The agricultural rescue policy was thwarted halfway. (4) The Manchurian policy was still wavering during the Seiyukai cabinet era, with the annexation policy or the establishment of a new protectorate still being debated. After Prime Minister Saito came to power, he immediately obeyed the military, recognized the Republic of Manchuria, and further created the Empire of Manchuria, implementing a protectorate policy, advocating an Asian Monroe Doctrine, and withdrawing from the League of Nations, seeking to dominate Asia.

In order to complete the above four major policies, Japan issued 2,481,850,000 yen in new public bonds during these three years. The domestic debt when Saito came to power (at the end of June 1932) was 4,986,000,000 yen, which had increased to 6,724,000,000 yen by April 1934, and reached 7,367,000,000 yen in March 1935. As for foreign debt, it exceeded 1,000,000,000 yen. This can also be said to be the achievements of the Saito cabinet in the past two years. (3rd United China Press)

At that time, Schleicher and his wife were in the living room. When they heard several rings of the bell, an unknown person ran out of the villa and hurriedly got into the car and left. This process took a very short time. Schleicher died immediately, and his wife was seriously injured in the abdomen and died on the way to the hospital. US Dockworkers' Strike Mediation Still Faces Many Twists and Turns 82

Forced Opening of Ports May Lead to Bloodshed

San Francisco: The West Coast Transportation Industry Strike Mediation Committee, appointed by the President, today placed the responsibility for peace or war on both labor and management, asking both parties to voluntarily request arbitration and abide by the arbitrator's decision. The committee declared, "In the opinion of this committee, if both parties request arbitration and abide by its decision, all disputes can be resolved peacefully." The committee also proposed that if striking workers return to their jobs, the arbitrator will conduct mediation. Today, two thousand striking workers gathered at the seaside at 3 PM, which was the date set by the California Industrial Association for the forced opening of the ports. However, the association announced that it had to postpone the opening until tomorrow because it was not fully prepared. All of this indicates that if both labor and management refuse arbitration, bloodshed may occur due to the forced opening of the ports. However, government mediators are still asking both parties to voluntarily request arbitration before Thursday. The attitude taken by the mediators has been explicitly approved by Labor Secretary Perkins. (National Telegraph on the 2nd)

Page 11

Disarmament Committee Approves Draft of Arms Trade Ban 83

(Geneva) The Committee for the Study of the Manufacture and Trade of Arms of the Disarmament Conference held a plenary meeting today to discuss the draft of the arms trade ban prepared by the Subcommittee on Arms Manufacture. (Note: The Committee for the Manufacture and Trade of Arms held a meeting on June 27, see the Geneva dispatch of that day for details.) The French representative explained that there are various difficulties in banning arms manufacture, such as the need for equal treatment between manufacturing and non-manufacturing countries, as well as between private and state-owned factories. The draft proposed by the subcommittee is sufficient to avoid various difficulties. He also explained the importance of realizing international supervision through public announcement. However, international supervision must take into account the special circumstances of arms manufacture and trade, so its implementation methods need to be carefully studied. The organization of supervision methods must also vary depending on the nature of the preparation. Some international supervision is carried out by supervising military expenditures, some by banning arms manufacture, and some by adopting other methods. Among these, it is necessary to seek mutual consideration. Representatives from the United Kingdom, Venezuela, Poland, Sweden, Czechoslovakia, Switzerland, and Spain all supported the subcommittee's draft, which was passed immediately without modification. (Havas dispatch on the 2nd)

Soviet Union Highly Interested in Ascending to the Stratosphere 84

Plans to Conduct Another Experiment in Late Summer

(Moscow) Scientists from the Soviet Union's Aviation and Chemical Defense Association today finalized plans to ascend to the stratosphere, a place above 25,000 meters where humans have never been. When the association first ascended last winter, the balloon was damaged, resulting in the death of three people. This time, they will conduct a detailed study to eliminate all shortcomings to prevent accidents. The date of the launch has not yet been decided, but it will likely take place in late summer, or it may be launched simultaneously with the balloon launch in the United States to compete. The purpose of this launch is to exceed the unofficial world record by 3,000 meters. The Soviet people are very interested in this launch and have contributed more than two hundred suggestions, some of the most valuable of which have been adopted.

Russian Scientists Explore Central Asian Desert 85

(Moscow) Today, a team of Soviet scientists departed from Moscow in a specially-made vehicle to explore the Karakum Desert in Central Asia. The expedition is led by Professor Miretsky, who is familiar with the area. It is expected to study fossils, pools of water, and the possibility of developing agriculture in the desert. The expedition will enter the desert from the north coast of the Caspian Sea, and the journey is expected to last about four months. (National Telegraph on the 3rd)

Cabinet Reshuffle in Cuba 86

Havana: The Cuban cabinet crisis was resolved last night. The list of new cabinet members is as follows: Minister of the Interior, Cuervo; Minister of Education, Fuertea; Minister of Finance, Landa (former Minister of Communications); Minister of Justice, Montalvo; Minister of Labor, Benitez. Benitez and Fuertea are not affiliated with any party. The other new cabinet members are all affiliated with President Mendieta's Nationalist Party. (Havas dispatch on the 3rd)

Provincial Governments in Bandit Suppression Provinces to Implement Joint Office 87

Chairman Chiang Reports to the Central Government

Vehemently Criticizes Current Administrative System's Common Problems

Nanchang Correspondence: Chairman Chiang has formulated a general outline for joint office by provincial governments, which has been reported to the Central Political Council for record. It will be implemented first in the bandit suppression provinces of Hubei, Henan, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian. The full text of Chiang's report to the Central Political Council and the telegraphic dispatch to the Executive Yuan, along with the general outline for joint office by provincial governments, is as follows:

Chiang's Telegraphic Dispatch 88

Chairman Chiang's report to the Central Political Council and telegraphic dispatch to the Executive Yuan stated: "The promulgation and implementation of the current provincial government organization law and county organization law have been in effect for several years. Although the provinces have formally completed their organization, in practice, there are many difficulties. They are like square pegs in round holes, completely incompatible. Therefore, reforming the local political system is a matter of urgency to refresh politics. The common problems of the current system can be summarized in three points: First, from the observation of the current system itself, it is top-heavy and lacks a solid foundation. In terms of organization, the province is large and the county is small. In terms of funding, the province is huge and the county is minuscule. There are too many agencies for governing officials and too few agencies for governing the people. There are too many high-ranking officials who do nothing and too few personnel who are deeply involved with the people. The greatest crux of the problem is that government orders become mere formalities. To compare the regular annual expenditure budgets for the four provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi in the 22nd year, the vast disparity between provincial and county administrative expenses is evident at a glance. Excluding the expenses of the Security Office, taking only the provincial government and the four departments as a standard, Henan has over 911,000 yuan, Hubei has over 1,119,000 yuan, Anhui has 1,010,000 yuan, and Jiangxi has over 813,000 yuan. The county administrative expenses in each of these provinces are: Henan, with 111 counties, has a total of over 1,091,000 yuan, averaging over 9,830 yuan per county; Hubei, with 70 counties, has a total of over 880,000 yuan, averaging over 12,600 yuan per county; Anhui, with 61 counties, has a total of over 957,000 yuan, averaging over 15,700 yuan per county; Jiangxi, with 81 counties, has a total of over 1,132,000 yuan, averaging over 13,800 yuan per county. Therefore, Anhui has the most county administrative expenses, followed by Jiangxi, then Hubei, and Henan has the least. However, in any province, the average monthly expenditure per county is only about one thousand yuan. The county is the mainstay of all government orders, and its importance is such, but the meager administrative expenses are as described above. There is no way to strengthen the organization, employ talent, or provide assistance. All efforts are abandoned, and this is naturally the case. Therefore, to reform the shortcomings of this top-heavy situation, the first step is to reduce the size of the provincial government's organization, expand the county government's organization, cut out the surplus of the provincial government, and transfer it to increase the county government's funding. Only by properly measuring the remedy can we promote benefits to the fullest extent. Second, from a horizontal perspective, the various departments and offices stand side by side, each forming its own system, each固守 its own scope, and each privatizing its own resources. Any matter under the jurisdiction of Department A is generally disliked by Department B. Matters involving two or more departments are often delayed and unresolved. They compete for power and shirk responsibility. Moreover, many measures are taken from the perspective of the respective department, lacking the spirit of suppressing oneself and promoting others to jointly maintain the overall situation. Thus, each recognizes the matters under its jurisdiction as the most urgent current affairs, and simultaneously supervises the county. The county magistrate does not know what to prioritize, and cannot do everything at the same time. As a result, the cunning ones specialize in perfunctory work, and the most unscrupulous ones borrow A to抵押 B, arbitrarily manipulating things to suit their own private plans. Those who are virtuous and cherish themselves suffer deeply from the disunity of government orders, are exhausted, and are uneasy in their positions. This kind of畸形 system is truly the厉阶 to the corruption of officialdom. Therefore, to eliminate the current stagnation, contradictions, duplication, segregation, and推諉 of provincial affairs, it is necessary to break the parallel situation of the various departments and merge them into a single, integrated provincial government. This will achieve the effect of uniformity, simplicity, harmony, and cooperation. Third, from a vertical perspective, the provincial government and its various departments and offices, and the county government and its various bureaus and sections, each form two distinct levels. The central ministries often recognize the provincial departments and offices as their directly subordinate agencies, and the provincial departments and offices also recognize the county bureaus and sections as their directly subordinate agencies. They directly communicate with each other in writing. The abuses resulting from this are that the provincial and county governments cannot exercise control at each level, and lose the effect of the body using its arms and the arms using its fingers. The regulations that the chairman represents the provincial government, supervises the execution of provincial affairs by subordinates, and that the county magistrate is in charge of the county's administration are mere words. The system is unclear and the levels are chaotic. How can we command subordinates and hold them accountable? Therefore, to eliminate this abuse, the entire provincial government must be absolutely responsible to the central ministries, and the entire county government must be absolutely responsible to the provincial government. The provincial departments and offices and the county bureaus and sections are auxiliary organizations of the province and the county and cannot be separated into two. All斜枝旁出的 writing methods should be resolutely abolished. In summary, the shortcomings of the current provincial system and the abuses arising from it are well known to those who understand the political situation today. They should be corrected and have become a unanimous request from above and below. However, a fundamental reform involves many things. If the central government considers only the current situation and changes the弦, it is deeply feared that there will be unforeseen consequences. There are two points that should be paid particular attention to. First, the various failures of the current provincial system are undeniable. In the future, the will of the provincial government should be unified, power should be concentrated, the organization should be tightened, and expenses should be saved. This is what the more knowledgeable people recognize. However, what is the appropriate degree of unification, concentration, tightening, and saving, and in what way should it be promoted? It is necessary to consider carefully and test it step by step. Second, the provinces of the country are vast and the relations are complex. The various situations of politics, culture, economy, and topography are not uniform. It is feared that it will be difficult to implement a uniform political system at the same time. For example, the设置 of four departments and two offices is considered too large in remote provinces and cannot be handled by manpower or financial resources. In the southeastern provinces, it is considered too simple and cannot meet the actual requirements without the addition of other specialized technical organizations. Even in terms of official ranks and salaries, the statutory salaries of the simplified任任 and appointed任任 are barely enough to maintain a livelihood in the southeastern provinces. If the定額 is paid in remote provinces, the entire department's expenses may only be enough to cover the salary of the主管長官. All these things are extremely disparate. The central system must be adapted to local conditions and considered over the long term. It seems that it is best to have a flexible and scalable local test. In recent years, Zhongzheng奉命 has supervised the troops and suppressed bandits. The more I have seen and heard, the more I have felt. I deeply believe that in order to promote local government affairs smoothly, especially the aftermath of bandit suppression in various provinces, it is necessary to unify the will of the provincial government and improve the efficiency of general administration. However, this kind of reform can only be carried out within the scope of not abandoning the current provincial government organization law and not affecting the budget of the provinces. Based on this principle, I have repeatedly discussed with the governments of the provinces for a year. Now, I have compiled the opinions of all parties and formulated a general outline of fourteen articles for the joint office of provincial governments. I have ordered the five provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian in the bandit suppression area to implement them as a test for the Central Government to thoroughly reform the local political system. In addition to分令, I have (correspondingly) enclosed the general outline for the review of the 钧会 and the checking of the 贵院, and I pray that it will be transferred (陈) to the National Government for record and implementation. This is a matter of public convenience."

Outline of Measures 89

The full text of the Provincial Government Joint Office Measures Outline is as follows: Article 1: Before the Central Government revises the current Provincial Government Organization Law, in order to strive for the advancement of local political affairs, maintain the unity of the provincial government's will, and improve the efficiency of general administration, this outline is specially formulated to implement the Provincial Government Joint Office Measures. All of the following departments shall be incorporated into the Provincial Government Office: 1. Secretariat, 2. Department of Civil Affairs, 3. Department of Finance, 4. Department of Construction, 5. Department of Education, 6. Security Department. Article 2: If the current Provincial Government Office does not have sufficient space to accommodate all subordinate departments, it should be incorporated as much as possible within the possible range, at least first incorporate the Department of Civil Affairs and the Security Department. The rest will be added successively after the government office is rebuilt and expanded. Regardless of whether it has been incorporated or not, the office procedures shall be handled in accordance with this outline. Article 3: In addition to the departments listed in Article 1, all current institutions directly under the provincial government should be abolished or reduced in size and transferred to the competent departments. If the aforementioned institutions are temporary organizations for the implementation of special key policies, their powers should be enhanced and treated as departments, and it would be more convenient to be directly under the jurisdiction of the provincial government, they may not be transferred for the time being, but should still be subject to the guidance of the competent departments. Article 4: After the provincial government's joint office, all documents shall be received and dispatched by the provincial government secretariat, and undertaken by the competent departments, and the chairman shall review and approve them with separate or joint countersignatures. However, the competent departments, in accordance with their powers, supervise and direct the affairs of their subordinate staff or agencies, and may still issue department orders or office orders within the scope of not conflicting with provincial orders. Article 5: After the provincial government's joint office, all departments under the provincial government shall not directly exchange documents with the central ministries and departments, or with the commissioners, county magistrates or mayors and their subordinate sections or bureaus, but shall act in the name of the provincial government. Article 6: After the provincial government's joint office, if the orders or punishments proposed by the departments have been issued in the name of the provincial government after being approved by the chairman, and it is discovered that they violate laws and regulations, exceed authority, or are otherwise inappropriate, they may be revised by themselves and suspended or revoked separately upon the proposal of the following and after the deliberation of the provincial government committee: 1. Proposed by the chairman of the provincial government, 2. Proposed by the director of the competent department, 3. Proposed by other department heads or committee members. Article 7: After the provincial government's joint office, thorough reforms should be carried out in accordance with the following principles: 1. The organization of each department and its subordinate agencies, as well as the responsibilities of each section and group, should be re-determined according to the actual needs, and abolitions and mergers should be strictly implemented to ensure a clear system, specialized powers and responsibilities, reduced staff, and intensive work. 2. The expenses of the provincial government and its departments should be centrally managed, but if it is temporarily inconvenient to completely centralize the accounting of money or goods, the scope of items should also be determined to centralize part or most of them first. 3. The documents of the provincial government and its departments should adopt scientific management methods to ensure speed, prudence and simplicity. The receipt, dispatch and undertaking of documents every day and every week should be classified and abstracted into lists and sent to the department heads and the chairman for review. However, this does not apply to particularly confidential matters that should not be announced temporarily, and the chairman and the competent departments should be solely responsible. Article 8: After the reorganization of the provincial government secretariat after the provincial government's joint office, in addition to abolishing the existing organization according to the provisions of the preceding article, and setting up sections to take charge of documents, accounting, general affairs, etc., the following offices may be established as appropriate, and personnel with special expertise should be used to form them: 1. Technology Office: For agricultural, industrial, commercial, mining, water conservancy, civil engineering and other projects that the province should urgently handle now, appropriate technical experts should be employed according to their types to be responsible for investigation and design. The technical matters proposed by the competent departments should also be submitted to them for review, and they should be responsible for guidance and supervision. 2. Legal System Office: For the laws and regulations proposed to be issued by the provincial government or its departments and the revision and abolition of current laws and regulations, those with special expertise should be employed and concentrated in the Legal System Office to be responsible for investigation, drafting and review. 3. Statistics Office: Establish statistical specialists. All materials that should be collected by various agencies shall be submitted to the Statistics Office to compile various statistical reports in accordance with uniform regulations. 4. Gazette Office: Establish translation and printing specialists. All periodic or irregular publications issued by various agencies shall be uniformly handled by the Gazette Office. All laws and regulations shall be announced daily in the gazette to save the trouble of writing and sending them. Article 9: After the thorough reform of the organization and staff of the provincial government and its departments, all the remaining expenses should be allocated to increase the county government expenses. The laid-off personnel should be re-identified, and their talents should be measured and allowed to be selected separately for the use of county magistrates, district chiefs and other county auxiliary officials. Article 10: The implementing rules of this outline shall be determined by the provincial governments of each province themselves. Article 11: This outline shall be reported to the Central Political Conference by the General Headquarters for review and record. It shall be implemented first in the bandit suppression provinces of Hubei, Henan, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian. Other provinces may also be approved to use it by analogy after submitting it to the Executive Yuan for approval. Article 12: After this outline is implemented in various provinces, the results of on-site trials should be compared in detail and reported to the central government at any time to prepare for the formulation of the provincial system and the implementation of the revised Provincial Government Organization Law for reference. Article 13: Matters not stipulated in this outline shall still be handled in accordance with the current Provincial Government Organization Law and other relevant laws and regulations. Article 14: This outline shall be implemented uniformly in all bandit suppression provinces within two months from the date of promulgation.

Leaders of Guangxi, Hunan and Guangdong Discuss National Defense Construction 90

Expand the Organization of the National Defense Construction Committee

Guangdong and Guangxi Share the Cost of Building the Sanhe Road

Guangzhou Correspondence, June 25th: Li Zongren, Bai Chongxi, and Chen Jitang visited He Jian at Tuisi Garden to discuss the national defense, bandit suppression, and transportation issues of the three provinces of Guangdong, Guangxi, and Hunan. The main points of their discussion are said to be: (1) The authorities of Guangdong, Guangxi, and Hunan provinces should eliminate the remaining bandits on the border of Hunan and Guangdong in a short period of time, and increase troops to jointly suppress the communist bandits in Jiangxi Province. (2) Actively open up the connecting lines of the three-province highways to facilitate the transportation of industry, commerce, and bandit suppression military affairs in the three provinces. (3) Guangdong, Guangxi, and Hunan will meet to deploy defense matters. (4) It is proposed to send personnel at any time, regardless of administrative divisions, to contact, inspect, study, and develop politics, security, economy, and industry. The results of the discussion were quite satisfactory, and it did not end until after 11 o'clock. It is also said that the Southwest National Defense Construction Committee intends to expand into a joint organization of five provinces. In addition to Guangdong, Guangxi, and Hunan, Guizhou and Fujian will be added. The regulations have been drafted by the Southwest Political Affairs Council. The number of members of the committee is tentatively set at nine, with the highest military and political leaders of each province as ex officio members. At present, the point that Guangxi Province pays the most attention to is the connection of the highway lines of the southwest provinces. The Guizhou-Guangxi Highway has already been completed. A few days ago, Li Zongren of Guangxi Province suggested at the Southwest Political Affairs Council that the Sanhe Railway from Sanshui County, Guangdong to He County, Guangxi should be built. The section of the road starts from Hekou in Sanshui, passes through Sihui, Guangning, Huaiji, and ends in He County, with a total length of more than 280 li. The survey has been completed. Bai Chongxi came to Guangdong this time to strongly promote its completion. He has repeatedly negotiated with Chen Jitang and Lin Yunying. As a result, the method of raising funds for road construction will be jointly borne by the Guangdong and Guangxi governments. The outline has been finalized. In the future, freight and passenger car fees will be levied, and surplus car profits will be allocated and stored as road construction funds, which will be separately repaid to the Guangdong and Guangxi governments. In addition, in order to connect the Hunan Province highway, Guangxi Province sent Li Fuguo, the section chief of the Guangxi Road Bureau, to Hunan a month ago to investigate Hunan's road administration and negotiate the issue of building a connecting line. It is planned to connect the Huangsha River to the border road line in northern Guangxi with the Hengyong Highway in Hunan Province. Moreover, since the Guangxi-Guizhou highway has already been connected, and the Guangxi-Yunnan highway has also been built in sections, it is planned to be completed in the 23rd year. However, the highways of Guangxi and Hunan provinces have not yet been connected. Once it is successful, the transportation of Yunnan, Guizhou, and Guangxi provinces can rely on the Hengyong line in Hunan Province to reach the Yangtze River. Hengyong and other places will become the transportation hub of the southwest. Moreover, the Hengyong route is only more than 200 li to the Guangxi border, and the cost is not very high. After consideration, the Hunan authorities believe that it is feasible and agreed to send personnel to work with the Guangxi Road Bureau to build the Hunan-Guangxi highway in a short period of time, implement connection and joint transportation (June 28).

Remnant Bandit Internal Strife: Luo Binghui Executed by Firing Squad 91

Luo Bandit Arrested on Suspicion of Social Democratic Party

All Bandits Panic and Gradually Disperse

Nanchang Correspondence: According to information from relevant sources, Gu Zheng, a refugee who fled from Ruijin yesterday, claimed that: (1) Luo Bandit Binghui, the commander of the pseudo-Fujian bandit area, was arrested and interrogated on suspicion of being a member of the so-called Social Democratic Party. It was believed that Luo Bandit indeed had reactionary behavior. He has been executed by firing squad by the pseudo-central government. Luo Bandit's department was panicked and surrendered to the National Army one after another. Other bandit departments also felt that their lips would be cold if their teeth were lost. They were suspicious of each other and gradually dispersed. (2) Bandit leader Zhu De is currently stationed in Changting, Fujian, etc. Also, the 35th Brigade of the 12th Division of the National Army dispatched a team to attack the bandits at Shuangxikou, Shangrao at 8:00 am on the 24th of last month. There were two or three hundred bandits in the area, and hundreds more were added at 10:00 am. They fought fiercely with the attacking troops of the National Army. Finally, the officers and soldiers fought bravely and defeated the bandits at 12:00 pm and occupied the high ground behind Shuangxikou. At 4:00 pm, the brigade dispatched infantry and artillery to attack Matoushan with the purpose of destroying the bandits in Qingshuitang. There were about one hundred bandits, and they fought hand-to-hand five times before and after. At 7:00 pm that day, the National Army occupied the mountain and took advantage of the situation to attack the Qingshuitang fortifications. The bandits still held their ground and tried to make a final struggle. They were finally broken through the deer fence by the officers and soldiers in the dark and completely occupied at 9:00 pm. A total of more than one hundred bandits were killed in the three attacks before and after that day, and many guns and weapons were seized. (July 2)

Gu Mengyu Issues Statement After Impeachment (Part 2) 92

(2) Regarding the original impeachment that should be defended

1. The original text stated that the Zhengtai Railway originally borrowed 40 million French francs, with a term of 30 years, and the principal and interest were repaid on schedule. It was repaid in full on March 1, 1932. The contract should be terminated and recovered for self-management according to the contract. However, Gu Mengyu delayed the acceptance and secretly continued to conduct material borrowing with the French representative Mardin (that is, the French side purchased materials on behalf of the borrower and settled accounts as cash, which would be repaid in installments, with half a year as one term and ten terms). When Mardin returned to France, he ordered material loans from Parisian electrical manufacturers, totaling 90 million French francs, for the purpose of expanding and repairing the Datong Road, which were divided into three batches for payment, with 50 million French francs as one batch, 25 million French francs as one batch, and 15 million French francs as one batch. A contract was signed for each batch, and on July 1, 1933, Gu Mengyu sent a representative to sign and establish it with the representative of the Parisian Electrical Factory, which caused the Zhengtai Railway to be formally recovered after a delay of one year. Fearing foreign criticism, the material loan contract was falsely called a material purchase contract. (It is said that several batches of the materials have arrived and are used by the western section of the Longhai Road and the Datong Road.) It was found that this material loan was secured by the income of the Zhengtai Railway, which had just been taken over, and the Chinese transportation and other Chinese merchant banking groups were also used as guarantees. In addition, the French Vinot was reappointed as the director of the Zhengtai Road Vehicle Department, and the French Bo Yan was appointed as the chief auditor of the Zhengtai Road and the chief engineer of the Datong Road. The Jiaotong and other banking groups also sent Wang Yizeng, the president of the Shijiazhuang Bank of Communications, as the road supervisor due to debt relations. The Zhengtai Road was nominally taken over, but the power was still in the hands of the French, and all the income was used as an unrestricted guarantee, and the conditions were particularly harsh. This is what the minister did for borrowing foreign loans regardless of the interests and losing national sovereignty, and he should be subject to disciplinary action. In addition to the points in the original text that are inconsistent with the facts, which have been reviewed and corrected by the supervisory committee member Yang Tianji and others, the statement that "the contract should be terminated, the contract should be terminated, the contract should be terminated, and the contract should be terminated. Such ignorant and speculative remarks came from the impeachment chapter of the Supervisory Committee member, which is really unfortunate. According to Article 5 of the Zhengtai Railway Loan Contract concluded with the Sino-Russian Daosheng Bank on October 15, 1902 (ie, September 14, Guangxu 28 of the former Qing Dynasty), the Ministry planned to hold the reception of the Zhengtai Railway on March 1, 1932, when the loan was repaid. However, the representative of the French Parisian Bank (the creditor's rights of the road were transferred from the Sino-Russian Daosheng Bank to the French Bank) and the French Embassy raised objections one after another, and the reasons they held were: (1) It is stated in Section 1 of Article 5 of the signed driving contract that it is valid for 30 years from the date of signing, and must be returned no earlier than October 15, 1932. (2) Since the European War, the Chinese government has repaid the 5% gold loan in 1902, all in paper francs, which is inconsistent with the regulations of the loan driving contract. According to the provisions on the borrowed ticket, it is required to repay in gold francs, but my country only paid paper francs. The 5% loan matter was not concluded until March 1, 1932, and so on, stating that they refused to transfer the road. After many negotiations, there was still no effect. At that time, the January 28th Incident occurred in Shanghai, and the diplomacy was urgent. This matter was related to the current situation, and the measures had to be taken carefully. Therefore, the proceedings were slightly delayed, and it was changed to a forcible takeover in mid-October. However, the French side has not yet recognized it. The situation of the takeover is not as the supervisory committee member said, it is only "a formal recovery", and "the power of Zhengtai is still in the hands of the French". There are not only many precedents for new-style industries in our country to employ foreign personnel, but also profitable and harmless. It has been 30 years since the Zhengtai Road was founded. The scale is strict, the management is perfect, and the income is complete. The expenditure is saved. Therefore, the principal and interest of the loan have been repaid on schedule. The reputation of the road is good, and the road letter is also high. A narrow-gauge railway of more than 200 kilometers has such achievements, and it can be called a model of Chinese railways. It is no shame. However, to promote its cause, most of it has to be attributed to the French personnel serving on the road. Not only are their achievements on the road excellent, but it is also appropriate to continue to appoint them after the takeover, so as to take advantage of the familiarity with the job. That is, considering their previous hard work, it is also appropriate to record and show that the Republic of China gives preferential awards to guest officials who are loyal to their duties. It is not appropriate to dismiss all of them on the day of recovery. This is the reason why the Ministry retained a part of the original French personnel after taking over the Zhengtai Road. As for the so-called "the power is still in the hands of the French", it is even more unknown what it is based on. The French personnel are all appointed by the Ministry of Railways. People have special duties, and duties have special responsibilities. They are bound by the regulations of the Ministry and listen to the command of the Bureau Director. At the end of each year, the Ministry awards and punishes them according to their achievements. If it is still said that "the power is in the hands of the French,"

Then, according to the supervisory committee member's intention, all foreign personnel in the central and local agencies must be dismissed. The original text also said that "all the income is used as an unrestricted guarantee, and the conditions are particularly harsh". It was found that the total value of the material purchase contract was 50 million French francs, equivalent to 10 million national currency, while the Zhengtai Railway's annual surplus was less than 2 million yuan, and other payments had to be deducted, and the net surplus was only more than 1 million yuan. If the entire amount is not used as a guarantee, according to the supervisory committee member's intention, how many parts should be used as a guarantee? It is "harsh" to use an income of more than 1 million yuan as a guarantee for 10 million yuan. According to the supervisory committee member's intention, what conditions are not harsh? This is what I would like the supervisory committee member to clarify and provide a solution.

2. The original text stated that the amount of this material loan reached 90 million French francs. Since it was named after the expansion and repair of the Datong Road, and it was known to be uneconomical construction funds, and harsh conditions that damage national sovereignty, it was impossible to obtain the consent of the Central Political Conference and the legislative body. Therefore, on the surface, it was called a material purchase loan, and contracts were signed in batches to reduce the amount, hoping to deceive the people and avoid the statutory procedures of submitting it to the Central Political Conference for approval and handing it over to the Legislative Yuan for review in accordance with the law. This is what the minister did to avoid the exercise of the powers of the Central Political Conference and the legislative body in violation of national law, and he should be subject to disciplinary action. The purchase of materials is different from borrowing money. The contract is a material purchase contract and cannot be forcibly called a loan contract. This level has been stated in the reply report of the supervisory committee members Yang Tianji and others, and will not be repeated here.

3. The original text stated that the so-called Datong Line has been under construction for nearly a year, only from Yuci, following the old Tongcheng Line to 35 kilometers between Taigu, the original earthwork, is being repaired, and the track is only five or six kilometers long (the track gauge is four feet and eight and a half inches, which is different from the Zhengtai Road track gauge of one meter. The Tongpu Road built by the Shanxi Ordnance Industry also starts from Taiyuan and passes through Yuci, Taigu, and ends in Jiexiu. The Zhengtai Road between Taiyuan and Yuci and the Datong Road between Yuci and Taigu face each other far away and become parallel lines with the closest distance. At this time, when the state-owned railways are in urgent need of expansion, about the important domestic transportation, there is more than just this road that urgently needs to be built. The minister borrowed huge amounts of foreign capital, but only for the construction of this parallel road line, first delaying the urgent and emphasizing the light, ignoring the overall situation, and acting inconsistently. Moreover, during the current construction period, he is wasting time and salaries. In the future, even if the road line is fortunately completed, it will lead to business competition due to the two parallel lines, and the result will be two failures. This is what the minister did to intentionally damage the interests of the country due to improper measures and should be subject to disciplinary action. It was found that most of the materials purchased this time were used on the Tongxi Line, not on the Datong Line. The review report of the supervisory committee members Yang Tianji and others has also stated this, and will not be repeated here. However, the statement that the Datong Line built by the Ministry and the Tongpu Line built by the Shanxi Provincial Ordnance Industry have become parallel lines, and the situation of their passage has to be slightly stated. The Tongpu Line from Datong to Puzhou in Shanxi, that is, the Datong Line from Datong to Tongguan, which the Ministry later called, is a trunk line running north and south in Shanxi, connecting the Longhai Line in the south and entering the PingSui Line in the north, and is also the main trunk line running north and south in the national railway network. According to the Ministry of Railways, a standard gauge should be built so that it can be connected to the national trunk lines and become a part of the national road network. In the spring of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, because the loan was hopeful, in order to promote early success, the Datong Road Engineering Office was organized in February of the 22nd year to start construction, and ordered the Zhengtai Road Bureau member to handle it concurrently, and directly subordinate to the Bureau to save expenses. However, before long, the Shanxi Provincial authorities also started construction of the narrow-gauge Tongpu Railway. The plan was not approved by the Ministry of Railways in advance. However, Director Yan telegraphed Yu when the Datong Road was just starting construction, briefly describing the plan for the light railway and requesting to order the roads to transport materials free of charge. Yu Dang replied to Director Yan on March 15 as follows: "Taiyuan Director Yan Baichuan, the Yuandian is respectfully known. After receiving the Jiangdian about the road construction problem in Jin Province, I have been waiting for a detailed letter to rely on research. On the one hand, I will inform Minister Li of this method and entrust him to transfer it, and I hope to get your listening. The Datong Road from Datong to Tongguan is now being actively carried out in the Ministry and will start construction soon. If you are building a light railway, it should be outside the scope of that road. As for the cement used for the light railway, it has been ordered to be exempted from transportation fees. Brother Gu Mengyu." After that, Director Yan sent Mr. Cui Wenzheng to Beijing to explain the Shanxi Provincial Ordnance Industry Road Construction Plan to Mengyu, so he sent Jiangdian to Director Yan again on April 3 as follows: "Taiyuan Director Yan Baichuan, according to Mr. Cui Wenzheng's oral description of the plan of the Zunzong's Ordnance Industry Road Construction, it will first build the line from Yuci South. It was found that this line is parallel to the Datong Railway, and the transportation business in the future will inevitably compete with each other, which is actually detrimental to both roads. In my opinion, the construction of the light railway by the Zunzong should focus on the nutrition line of the state-owned trunk road. Since the Datong Road is the north-south line, the light railway should be the east-west line, such as the line from Pingyao to the west, the line across east and west from Lingshi, and the line from Qinghuazhen to the west into southern Jin. If they can be built one after another, they can cooperate with the state-owned trunk line and help each other. This is my humble opinion, and there may be some places that can be adopted. I hope you will cut it down for good fortune. Brother Gu Mengyu." Director Yan failed to follow the above opinion, and then the Ministry received a report from the Datong Road Engineering Office in May, saying (1) Director Yan started to build the Yuci-Xugou line, which is almost parallel to the Datong Line, on April 13 (2. The houses needed by the Datong Road Engineering Office for office and accommodation of staff and company members are now occupied by the army building the above-mentioned roadbed. After that, the difficulty of the Tian Tong Road Engineering Office increased day by day. After repeated consultations, Director Yan only agreed to dismantle the narrow-gauge Tongpu Road after the standard gauge Datong Road was completed, but stated that the Provincial Tongpu Road will continue as before before the Datong Road handled by the Ministry is completed. The Ministry saw that the technical and economic and other difficulties could not be solved, so it ordered the Datong Engineering Office to temporarily suspend work, and the materials originally ordered for the road were all transferred to other lines. The above is the process of the Datong Line being built and then stopped. The supervisory committee member Liu Houwu did not observe the situation and made arbitrary criticisms. It is true that he claimed to be "ignorant of the overall situation and acting inconsistently."

4. The supervisory committee member said, "Some commentators said that there are many shady scenes in this material purchase, and the sophistication of the profiteering and the amount of embezzlement are worse than the loan kickbacks in the Beijing government era. People are talking about it, and there is a reason for it." The committee member Liu Houwu is not only confused and does not observe the facts, but also creates such baseless rumors and uses the destruction of other people's reputation as his business. But if the country has a common law and society has good customs, this kind of rumors, once uttered from a private person's mouth, has constituted the crime of defamation. Today, with the dignity of the Supervisory Yuan, it exercises its powers, presents an impeachment chapter, and publishes it publicly, which is forbidden by the laws of civilized countries and not allowed by customs. I can't help but grieve for the future of the Supervisory System of our country. (End)
