Northwest Inspection Notes

The Rich Resources of Ningxia in Water Conservancy, Agriculture, and Mining 97

The Helan Mountains in Ningxia stand tall, able to block cold air and drifting sands. The rivers are at a high elevation, providing irrigation benefits. The soil is fertile, and the products are abundant. It has naturally received unique advantages, and human construction continues to strive. The title of "Heavenly Prefecture on the Frontier" has been increasingly enhanced in its value. Now, according to Director Yu Jieyi of the Department of Construction, I will briefly discuss the water conservancy, agriculture, forestry, industry, commerce, and products of Ningxia Province, as follows:

Since the Han and Tang dynasties, Ningxia has opened canals to draw water and reclaimed land for colonization, transforming a barren land into a fertile area. However, the land contains alkali, making it suitable for irrigation but not for excessive rain. Excessive rain causes the alkali to rise to the surface, making the soil hard and poor, harming the crops. Irrigation, on the other hand, brings silt with the river water, suppressing the alkali. With the application of some fertilizer, the soil becomes fertile. In the eighteenth year of the Republic [1929], Shaanxi and Gansu suffered a drought, and starvation was widespread. Ningxia alone sang of abundance, which is the reason for this. There are ten major canals in the entire province: Hanyan Canal, opened during the Han dynasty, unknown year, 195 li long, passing through Ningxia and Shuofang counties, irrigating over 128,000 mu of land; Tanglai Canal, created in the Tang dynasty, 320 li long, passing through Ningxia, Shuofang, and Pingluo counties, irrigating over 179,000 mu of land; Huinong Canal, opened in the fourth year of the Yongzheng reign of the Qing dynasty, 262 li long, passing through Ningxia, Shuofang, and Pingluo counties, irrigating over 111,400 mu of land; Daqing Canal, opened in the forty-seventh year of the Kangxi reign of the Qing dynasty, 71 li long, passing through Ningxia, Shuofang, irrigating over 16,200 mu of land; Tianshui Canal, opened in the thirty-fourth year of the Guangxu reign [1908], 30 li long, passing through Ningxia, irrigating over 6,000 mu of land. The above five canals are located on the west bank of the Yellow River. Qin Canal, created in the Qin dynasty, 150 li long, passing through Lingwu County, irrigating over 700 mu of land; Han Canal, created in the Han dynasty, repaired in the Qing dynasty, 100 li long, passing through Jinji, irrigating 125,800 mu of land; Meili Canal, opened in the Renwu year of the Jiajing reign of the Ming dynasty [1522], passing through Zhongwei, 200 li long, irrigating over 45,000 mu of land; Qixing Canal, opened in the Ming dynasty, 140 li long, passing through Zhongning, irrigating over 27,800 mu of land; Changrun Canal, opened in the fourth year of the Yongzheng reign of the Qing dynasty, 130 li long, passing through Pingluo, irrigating over 1,690 mu of land. In total, about 711,000 mu of land are irrigated. Although Ningxia has a large amount of fertile land as mentioned above, the wilderness awaiting development is many times greater. Recently, the General Bureau of Land Reclamation has investigated and found over 870,000 mu of wasteland that is extremely suitable for reclamation and cultivation. The distribution areas are roughly as follows: (1) Dengkou County: This county, from Dengkou in the east, the Wula River in the west, the Helan Mountains in the south, and the Yellow River in the north, has an area of about 1,000 square li, totaling over 500,000 mu. It was formerly under the direct jurisdiction of the A-Jie-Shan Banner. Since the Gengzi Incident [Boxer Rebellion], the indemnity for the church has not been cleared, and it has been managed by foreigners. Canal opening and land reclamation have already yielded over 100,000 mu of good land. Each year, they only pay a rent of over 10,000 yuan to the A-clan prince's residence, while the income reaches about 400,000 yuan. The Gengzi indemnity for the church was only a few hundred yuan, and the treaty period expired in the nineteenth year of the Republic [1930]. Urgent negotiations should be conducted to recover it and renew the lease with the prince's residence. This would both recover rights and interests and increase income. In addition to the cultivated land irrigable by canals, the county still has over 300,000 mu of uncultivated wasteland. If canals and ditches are opened, it will immediately become fertile land. (2) Zhenshuo Fort in Pingluo County: This fort is located near the Zhannen Canal (a branch of the Tanglai Canal), east from Shuangdunzi, west to Chongkou Fort, south from the Erdao Canal (a small branch of the Zhannen Canal), and north to Guanhudun, with an area of about 400 square li. Approximately 200,000 mu of wasteland can be reclaimed. If the Zhannen Canal is extended further, passing through Zhenshuo Fort and entering the river at Shizuishan, about 200 li long, another 300,000 mu of wasteland can be reclaimed, totaling over 500,000 mu. (3) Hezhong Fort in Ningxia County: This fort is east from the Qin Canal, west to the Yellow River, about 15 li long, south from Xinjiabao, and north to the Yellow River, about 20 li long. Excluding the desert canals, buildings, and over 10,000 mu of cultivated land, about 700 mu of wasteland can still be reclaimed. In total, the reclaimable wasteland mentioned above amounts to 870,000 mu. Assuming that each person reclaims 20 mu of wasteland, 43,500 people can be accommodated. If all the land is successfully reclaimed, the annual public and private income, calculated at 6 yuan per mu, could reach over 5 million yuan. However, the cost of opening canals, building villages, purchasing farming tools, etc., during reclamation totals over 3.6 million yuan. This cannot be achieved without a comprehensive plan and concerted effort from the government and local authorities.

Ningxia's natural forests, located in the passes of the Helan Mountains, are estimated to have about 200,000 trees, Pingluo has 160,000 trees, and Ningxia has 100,000 trees. During the Qing dynasty, they were protected by the Green Standard Army. Since the Republic, felling has been arbitrary, and they have gradually become scarce. Artificial forests have not been established. In the eighteenth year of the Republic [1929], the construction of the province was reorganized, and the Department of Construction also managed rivers and water conservancy. It began to preserve and expand the trees on the canal dikes and established nurseries on the silted land along the rivers to promote afforestation. Since Director Yu took office, he has personally supervised the staff in the department and instructed all counties to plant trees uniformly during each Arbor Day. The Construction Bureau is strictly ordered to patrol each section. In recent years, the number of surviving trees has become increasingly impressive. The desolate situation of the past has gradually transformed into a lush scene.

The province has fertile land for thousands of miles, and its products are abundant. It is not only suitable for farming and grazing but also convenient for industry and commerce. Products such as salt, alkali, fur, saltpeter, licorice, and medicinal materials have large annual yields, making it a naturally endowed industrial zone. Cattle, sheep, camels, and horses thrive everywhere. Tan sheep fur is famous throughout the country. Wool carpets are also as renowned as the products from Baotou. However, the annual production of various animal skins is approximately 140,000 pieces. Apart from being used locally for making boxes, the majority, along with the annual production of over 1 million jin of camel and sheep wool, has always been transported by merchants to Tianjin, resold to foreign merchants, made into finished products, and then resold to China. The extent of this leakage is extreme. The Department of Construction initially established an industrial testing ground, and now it is being expanded to produce leather, boots, shoes, carpets, wool yarn, weaving, soap, dyeing, and other materials. Among these, leather boots and shoes are produced in increasing quantities, and sales are gradually expanding. The annual production of licorice is approximately 2 million jin, of which about 300,000 to 400,000 jin are sold to foreign countries (such as Japanese Jintan, tobacco, and Finnish and German medicinal uses). A Finnish merchant named Willio Voss invented a machine to boil it into paste locally and transport it to foreign countries, making huge profits. However, he stopped due to heavy taxes. Currently, there is still a merchant-run Yuning Licorice Company that boils it using machines, but foreign sales are not as smooth as before.

Mineral production is dominated by coal, while other mineral resources have not been explored. It is said that all kinds of metals are found in the territories of the Alxa and Ejina Mongol banners. However, due to the lack of guidance from specialized talent and the enterprise of capitalists, the resources are abandoned on the ground and cannot be exploited. Salt and alkali are natural crystals and are produced in abundance. The Huamachi, Huianchi, Gouchi, Lannichi, and Lianhuachi, etc., crystallize into salt once a year. The major salt lakes in the Mongolian areas of Alashan, Dingyuanying, Chaghan, Nalin, and Hamagatai Nuo, etc., are also naturally formed, only with larger grains and higher yields. The annual salt production in the above areas totals 200 to 300 million jin. Natural alkali lakes are even more numerous. The method of mining is only to send workers to the lake to dig it out in winter and spring. Each block weighs several hundred jin and is transported to the province and Shaanxi and Gansu. If new methods can be adopted to produce pure, slag-free alkali blocks, it is hoped that the import of foreign alkali can be resisted. Furthermore, using chemical methods to extract sodium carbonate and caustic soda can provide raw materials for the chemical industry. It is estimated that the three major alkali lakes in Etoke Banner (see previous grassland communications) can produce about 20 million jin of alkali annually. Baijinaer produces about 60,000 jin annually. Most of the rest crystallizes and dissolves on its own, and no one investigates. There are even cases where Mongolians consider them sacred lakes and do not allow mining.

Ningxia has four major specialties: some refer to lake salt, lake alkali, fur, and licorice, while others refer to Chinese wolfberry, licorice, Tan sheepskin, and chazi (coal slack). Although there are slight differences, each has its reasons. Salt and alkali are naturally abundant products, Chinese wolfberry and licorice are warm and nourishing medicines, Tan sheepskin has up to thirteen bends in its fur, and chazi is a type of coal that is very similar in nature to charcoal and is extremely easy to burn. If covered with ash, it will not go out for a long time. If buried in a pit in large chunks, it can stay hot for fifty to sixty days. However, it is best to avoid the initial fumes. In addition to the well-known Chinese wolfberry and licorice, medicinal materials also include astragalus, codonopsis pilosula, angelica sinensis, and musk, etc. Fruits include grapes, pears, peaches, dates, pomegranates, and walnuts, etc. Agricultural products include wheat, corn, sesame, peas, sorghum, and millet, all produced locally. Rice is produced in paddy fields and can be transported to the Long province [Gansu].

The National Economic Commission's Jiangxi Office is Working 98

Carrying out Various Rural and Health Construction Projects

Nanchang Correspondence: The National Economic Commission has established an office in Jiangxi, which was officially established on May 23. The newly appointed director of the commission, Xiao Chunjin (formerly chairman of the Jiangxi Provincial Economic Commission), has also reported to the National Economic Commission for duty and has begun construction according to the plans set by the Economic Commission. The progress of the project is briefly described as follows:

Agricultural Technology: Jiangxi's agricultural technology remains in the state of the Middle Ages. The institution responsible for improvement is the Agricultural College, which is divided into five departments: plant production, animal production, agricultural extension, rural economy, and rural education. All agricultural agencies in the province are under its command. The college site has been located near the Liantang Rural Normal School. The Economic Commission has allocated 200,000 yuan, and the Provincial Government has allocated 120,000 yuan for all equipment. It is currently under construction.

Agricultural Economy: Jiangxi's cooperative business has made rapid progress in recent years. More than 800 cooperatives of various types have been established. New ones are emerging like mushrooms. However, in the past, emphasis was placed on credit cooperation. The purpose of this office is to develop Jiangxi's production and increase exports. In the future, special attention will be paid to transportation cooperation. For example, the province's specialty products such as paper, ramie cloth, timber, and handicrafts such as porcelain will be organized for cooperative transportation and sales to facilitate the flow of goods, and the economy will naturally prosper. The Economic Commission has allocated 500,000 yuan as a cooperative fund to be lent to various societies to serve as capital.

Rural Service: The office has divided the province into ten areas as rural improvement experimental zones. It will temporarily concentrate its efforts on various businesses in Zhangshe, Shangdun, and the countryside of Nancheng, including cooperation, health, sideline occupations, and technological improvements. After success, it will be promoted and popularized. In the past, everything emphasized urban construction, resulting in distorted development. Ninety percent of the total financial revenue was taken from farmers, but not a penny was used for rural relief and construction. The future emphasis on rural construction will correct this shortcoming.

Health Construction: The Provincial Health Department has been established. Director Pan Ji has received 300,000 yuan in construction funds from the Economic Commission. First, a model provincial hospital will be built on the site behind the Gongyuan [Examination Hall]. The equipment fee is more than 300,000 yuan. In the future, it will be the only hospital in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. A health center has been established in Nanchang City to improve environmental hygiene. Other counties are also strictly implementing health administration and establishing hospitals to reverse the declining population. (June 30)

Fujian Province's Recovered Bandit Areas Establish Rural Villages 99

Establishing Farmers' Banks to Lend Funds

The Headquarters Allocated 500,000 Yuan as a Fund

Fuzhou Correspondence: The bandit areas of Fujian Province now only include Changting, Ninghua, Mingxi, and Qingliu counties. Jiang Dingwen, Commander-in-Chief of the East Route Army, has specially dispatched his plenipotentiary representative, Jiang Bocheng, to Guangdong to discuss joint suppression measures with Chen Jitang, Commander-in-Chief of the South Route Army. It has been decided that the remaining bandits in the Fujian-Jiangxi border area will be attacked simultaneously by the East, North, and South Route Armies. It is expected to be launched within a few days. Currently, the total number of Red bandits in Fujian and Jiangxi is more than 50,000, with about 20,000 in the four counties of Fujian Province and about 30,000 in the five counties of Jiangxi Province. They are extremely scattered internally. Once attacked by the three-route armies, it will not be difficult to wipe them out completely. Therefore, clearing the bandit atmosphere is no longer a problem. However, the fields and gardens in the recovered counties are desolate, the houses are in ruins, the people have fled, and the local area has been completely devastated. Without a comprehensive post-disaster solution, it will be impossible to restore social vitality. If the refugees are simply recruited back to their hometowns without planning for their livelihoods, it will be difficult to make them settle down. In response to the actual needs, the Provincial Government has specially organized a Rural Committee for the Restoration of Bandit-Affected Counties, headed by Li Zuyu, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, Xu Fu, Director of the Department of Finance, and Chen Ticheng, Director of the Department of Construction, to be responsible for handling the matter. The method is to establish a Farmers' Bank in the provincial capital and offices in the bandit-affected counties. On the one hand, the county government orders all districts and villages to organize credit cooperatives. The cooperatives borrow funds from the bank offices to purchase agricultural tools and store them in the cooperatives. Any farmer who has returned to his hometown after fleeing and wants to cultivate the land but does not have agricultural tools or seeds can ask for a guarantor to purchase them on credit from the cooperative and repay them in installments after the harvest. This is the first step in restoring the countryside. However, the fund for this Farmers' Bank must be at least 500,000 yuan. However, after the counties have been successively recovered, it is necessary to establish county governments and to prepare for post-disaster relief. The need for funds is enormous. At this time when Fujian Province's finances are difficult, it is really difficult to raise this huge amount. Therefore, Director of Finance Xu Fu used the opportunity to attend the National Finance Conference to present the situation to the Central Government and the Nanchang Headquarters and requested assistance. Yesterday, the Provincial Government received a telegram from Xu Fu stating that the Headquarters had approved an allocation of 500,000 yuan as a fund for the Farmers' Bank, and the Ministry of Finance had also approved an additional 50,000 yuan per month to the original subsidy of 250,000 yuan for local post-disaster relief expenses. The authorities are quite satisfied with this. It is expected that the Farmers' Bank will be established after Xu Fu returns to Fujian. However, the refugees who have returned to their hometowns are in dire need of relief and cannot wait. The Restoration Committee has specially received 60,000 yuan from the Provincial Government to purchase 10,000 bags of rice in Shanghai and transport them to the bandit-affected areas for flat-price sales to provide emergency relief. At the same time, the committee will send personnel to various counties to investigate the local disaster situation in order to prepare for post-disaster relief. (19th)

Songjiang County Chamber of Commerce Requests Continued Dredging of the River 100

The County Chamber of Commerce held a joint routine meeting of executive supervisors on the 3rd morning. Committee member Lu Shulian proposed that the dredging of the river in the urban area has been suspended, the riverbed has cracked, the food and drink are smelly, commercial transportation is blocked, and the epidemic is spreading. How can we take action to send a telegram to the provincial authorities to expedite the dredging and urgently plan preventive measures? The reason is briefly stated as follows: The dredging of the river in the urban area is urgently needed by all the citizens. However, it was suspended abruptly after starting work in the east outside the city. As a result, the riverbed is completely exposed in the area from the city center to Dama Road Bridge, and cracks have appeared, causing many obstacles. During this dredging, the construction methods and the progress of the project were all the responsibility of the county government. However, it was immediately suspended, although it was due to the attacks of some people. However, the focus of the dispute is on the poor methods, not on the suspension of dredging. How can we stop eating because of choking and make the city river, which the 80,000 people of Song have been expecting to be dredged, stop in anger and lead to a terrible state of drinking water for the whole city? I respectfully propose that this be discussed and decided by a public vote. Resolution: (A) To be in accordance with the current situation, (1) Send a telegram directly to the provincial authorities, (2) Send letters to the overseas hometown associations to ask for assistance, (3) Recommend Cheng Weiru, Lu Shulian, Zhu Yian, and Sun Shaochi to petition the county government, (B) To comply with the standards, (1) Add it to the current medical bureau and organize vaccinations for epidemic prevention in advance. The remaining cases are omitted.

The Tinglin Lantern Festival Incident Ends 101

Since the spring, the lantern festival has been enthusiastically held in the four rural villages of this county, with a sudden surge of activity. However, the Tinglin festival was stopped by the district chief notifying the local public security bureau, resulting in a conflict in which the lanterns of the late president's portrait and the national flag were destroyed. The fellow villagers in Beijing telegraphed the provincial authorities to thoroughly investigate. The provincial government ordered the county to investigate and report on the circumstances of the incident. After investigation, it was found that nothing of the sort had happened. After receiving the report, the provincial government instructed that the district chief, Zhang Baotai, be recorded with a demerit. However, the police officers in charge of the public security bureau are responsible for maintaining public order and failed to find a way to eliminate the problem, which cannot be excused. The county magistrate will deal with them separately. At the same time, in accordance with the order of the Department of Civil Affairs No. 5842, the allegations of police corruption made by Zhou Shizhen and others will be investigated in detail as soon as possible, and the director of the public security bureau will be supervised to rectify the situation and report it together for inspection and punishment.

Suzhou

Extremely Hot Weather and Epidemic 102

Since the heavy rain on the evening of the 1st, the climate has suddenly become extremely hot, breaking the previous days' records. The river water has become increasingly dry and turbid, leading to a severe epidemic in the Xupan area on the 2nd, with successive deaths, reaching more than a dozen people. Cases have also been found on Dongzhong City Main Street. However, there is no news about the organization of epidemic prevention hospitals. Yesterday (the 3rd) afternoon, the thermometer in the room was 103 degrees Fahrenheit. The hot and stuffy weather made residents feel extremely uncomfortable.

Trial Opens for Murder of Temple Keeper 103

The case of Wang Jinsheng, the temple keeper of the Maoshantang Temple outside the door, being brutally killed by his son-in-law, Chen Wanquan, in collusion with his wife, Wang Pan, was publicly tried by the local court at 10:00 a.m. on the 3rd. The deceased's son, Genbao, daughter Zhangjin, neighbor Yang Laohu, and Jin Bingjun, the patrol leader of the Third-Fifth Precinct, were summoned to court. Judge Zhu Jun presided over the trial. Genbao still testified in court that his mother and brother-in-law had brutally killed his father. Zhangjin claimed to be unaware. The defendants, Chen Wanquan and Wang Pan, still denied killing Wang Jinsheng. As a result, the trial was postponed for further investigation. Wang Pan and Chen Wanquan were returned to custody.

Su Bingwen Leaves Suzhou for Beijing 104

General Su Bingwen brought his family to Suzhou after the end of the Northeast war and lived in Wumen for a year. He spent his days leisurely with poetry and wine and did not ask about external affairs. Recently, he received a telegram from Chairman Chiang summoning him to Beijing to inquire about everything. He will be entrusted with an important military post. After Su returned to Suzhou, he prepared everything and left Suzhou for Beijing with his family yesterday (the 3rd).

Wuxi

Farmers Suffer from Drought and Pray for Rain 105

The city has been hot and stuffy for a week. Yesterday (the 2nd), the indoor temperature was still above 103 degrees Fahrenheit. At about 7 p.m. in the southwest corner, dark clouds gathered, and lightning flashed. After half an hour, a strong wind suddenly arose, and the treetops danced, with the potential for thunderstorms. At 8:15, large raindrops began to fall, but after only two or three minutes, the rain suddenly stopped, the wind blew the clouds away, and the sky was full of twinkling stars. There was no sign of rain. The whole night was hot and stuffy, and the people were greatly disappointed. Today (the 3rd), the heat is even worse. If it does not rain again, the crops will be hopeless. The blind people in the county are extending monks at Huangbudun to recite scriptures and chant prayers for rain. The Red Swastika Society has been reciting Buddhist scriptures for ten days. Shen Bo'an, a fortune teller in Jiangyin Lane, is also extending Taoists and Buddhist nuns at home to recite scriptures and pray for rain, and he has also made a grass dragon and hired people to pick it up and walk around praying for rain. Farmers in the countryside are praying for rain on the dry riverbeds. The county magistrate originally intended to stop slaughtering animals immediately, but he has delayed implementation due to the slaughter tax. A large turtle in the gutter of the house of the township chief of Houqiao Township made a strange cry. A large turtle in the well of a certain family in Anzhen wanted to get out of the well. The villagers said that this was a sign of a great drought. The number of people suffering from heatstroke has been increasing in recent days, and the hospitals are extremely busy. Xing Yuantang, a prison guard in the county, in order to appease the prisoners, specially submitted a list of 50 people, including Chen Rongsheng, who met the bail regulations to the county for review so that bail procedures could be processed as soon as possible. County Magistrate Yan Shenyu has also scheduled a meeting to discuss the rice price issue. Qian Sunqing, director of the County Financial Property Office, requested the opening of the Lugang River. Epidemics are very prevalent in urban and rural areas, especially in rural areas, which are the most miserable, without doctors or medicine, which is quite pitiful.

Organizing Local Donation Collection Office 106

The county government held its 19th administrative meeting at 10:00 a.m. yesterday. County Magistrate Yan, as chairman, decided on important cases: (1) All expenses before the 22nd year of the Republic [1933] shall be settled by all agencies before July 15, and the statements shall be reported to the county in advance. (2) In accordance with the order of the Department of Finance, a local donation collection office shall be organized. (3) Qian Jihou, director of the County Financial Property Office, submitted a letter on the proposed supplementary measures for receiving the municipal financial property association. In addition to the previous resolutions of the administrative meeting, it was decided: (A) The location will still be at the original site of the municipal financial property association. (B) All paintings, calligraphy, and miscellaneous items in the park will be inventoried and registered by the park management committee and sent to the financial property office for record. (C) The Municipal Engineering Office is abolished. (4) Epidemic prevention expenses will be handled as before. (5) The weather is extremely dry, and the price of rice is rising daily. Efforts should be made to provide relief. It was decided to send letters to the Chamber of Commerce and various associations of grain and soybean merchants to schedule a meeting to discuss measures.

Changzhou

Extremely Hot and Long Drought, Stop Slaughtering Animals and Praying for Rain 107

Wuyi County has been even hotter in recent days, and it is still not raining. The crops in the four rural villages will be hopeless. When the county government convened an administrative meeting on the 2nd, it was proposed that there has been a long drought, and the farmers are eagerly awaiting rain. It is urgent to stop slaughtering animals in order to hope for a great rain and comfort the people's expectations. Is this appropriate? Please make a public decision. It was decided that from the 4th of this month, slaughtering will be stopped throughout the city and rural areas for seven days. If there is heavy rain during this period, the ban will be lifted. A public notice will be issued immediately, and the slaughter tax collectors will be notified to comply, otherwise, they will be severely punished.

It has been more than 20 years since the Grand Canal was dredged in the early years of the Republic. It has been heavily silted. Every winter, the river water is even shallower, and boats are crowded. Currently, there is a severe drought, and the rice fields are cracked. Irrigation for hundreds of thousands of acres of farmland along the river is impossible. After County Magistrate Bao inspected the situation, he planned to dredge the Grand Canal at the same time as opening the Huangtiangang. After the County Construction Committee decided, the situation was reported to the Department of Construction for approval.

Yang She Town Fire 109

The home of Zhou Yousheng, west of the fortress wall of Yang She Town, Fourth District, suddenly caught fire at 11 a.m. yesterday (the 1st) due to children playing with fire. The weather was hot and there was a long drought with no water to extinguish the fire. It was allowed to burn to as many as 17 homes, destroying a total of 37 houses. It took three hours to extinguish the fire, resulting in heavy losses.

Jiashan

Two Suicide Cases 117

Zhang Fusheng from Xiaotongwei, Xitang Town in our county, is currently serving as a patrolman in the 7th Platoon of the Water Police. Several years ago, he adopted a daughter named Xiaofeng. Later, he took in a son-in-law who started a business in a Pinghu freight shop after the marriage. The other day at night, Xiaofeng was scolded and beaten by her adoptive father over some matter. Xiaofeng, filled with resentment and indignation, secretly sought death and died. At the same time, a nephew of Zhang, Ru from Chengmengqiaoxia Pond, was apprenticed in a bran shop. This time, he was entrusted with carrying funds to purchase goods at a certain place. On the way through his hometown, he was persuaded by relatives and friends to stay overnight and play mahjong. Unexpectedly, Zhang suffered consecutive losses and lost all the funds he was carrying. He then borrowed from his sister to cover the debt, but his sister refused. He hanged himself.

Reports of Severe Drought and Famine Arrive One After Another 118

Our county has not seen rain for nearly two months. The fields are cracked, and the seedlings are withered. Coupled with the continuous scorching heat, with temperatures reaching 108 degrees on the thermometer, the scorching sun is like fire, with a red umbrella held high. Farmers are working day and night to scoop water, but it is like a drop in the bucket and does not help the situation. The fields in the second district of the county, which are at a higher elevation, are suffering even more. In the past few days, farmers from Heping Township, Dongbei Yunwei, and Jiunan District, Luziwei, have submitted famine reports, arriving like snowflakes. Furthermore, the County Farmers' Association held an emergency meeting yesterday to address the withering of crops due to the drought and requested the county government to send personnel to conduct on-site surveys and plan relief measures as soon as possible to alleviate the suffering of the people.

Execution of a Major Opium Trafficker by Firing Squad 119

Chen Ziqing (also known as Cheng Ziqing), the owner of the Shenzhou Hotel in Hangzhou City, trafficked large quantities of opium, using the home of Fan Hongzhang at No. 51 Pishi Lane as his base. The police局 cracked the case and seized more than 1,200 taels of opium, arresting Fan and sentencing him. Chen escaped and was not apprehended. Recently, Chen sneaked back to Hangzhou and was captured by the Security Office, sent to the court, and confessed without reservation. He was sentenced to death. The sentence was submitted to the Provincial High Court and approved by the Provincial Government. This morning (the 3rd) at 8:00 AM, the prisoner was brought to the Xishi Market and executed by firing squad. His wife prepared a coffin to collect his body.

Suicide of the Director of the Beiping Drama Troupe 120

Fang Kui (also known as Xingju), the director of the Beiping Xinghua New Drama Troupe, was 26 years old. Previously, he went south from Beiping to Shanghai, but failed to find employment. Later, he came to Hangzhou to visit a friend but did not meet them. In despair, he wrote two suicide notes in a hotel yesterday. In the afternoon, at the Third Bridge of the Su Causeway on West Lake, he tore up the letters, business cards, diary, and several pawn tickets from Tianjin Yide Pawnshop and Shanghai Fuchang and Xinkai Pawnshops, wrapped them in a handkerchief, placed them on the bridge, and jumped into the lake. People saw him but were unable to rescue him in time, and he died. The incident was reported to the court for inspection and a coffin was prepared.

Ningbo

The Daishan Ferry is Robbed and Pillaged 121

The Daishan Ferry, operated by the Xiangshan Company on the Jiangbei Bank of this port, which runs between Ningbo and Shengshan, was sailing from Shengshan to Ningbo at 7:00 AM on the 28th of last month. Unexpectedly, two bandits disguised as passengers boarded the ship. When the ship departed from Sijiao, five more bandits, each concealing a handgun, boarded. At around 4:00 PM on the 29th, when the ship was passing near Huanglongkou, Chaishanyang, the seven bandits shouted and pulled out their handguns, taking control of the wheelhouse and engine room, forcing the captain to sail to the bottom of Taohua Mountain. They fired shots as a warning, wounding sailor He Caipin in the right foot and injuring tea boy He Xinzhang and sailor Li Li. As a result, clothing, luggage, and silver dollars worth about 2,000 yuan were robbed, and the comprador He Jintang, accountant Wu Asi, and passenger Mr. Chen from Sizhou were kidnapped. The bandits left the ship at around 3:00 AM in the evening. The ship escaped danger and arrived in Ningbo at 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon, and requested the Security Branch and the 2nd Detachment of the Water Police to investigate and rescue them.

Jiaxing

Verdict in the Police-Civilian Conflict Case 122

The police-civilian conflict that occurred in Jiaxing on the night of March 4th, resulting in the shooting death of Shen Jinguan and injuries to several others, was investigated by Li Zhongjun, Chief Prosecutor of the local branch court. He filed a public prosecution based on three parts: murder, encroachment, and obstruction of official duties. Judge Zhou Wending repeatedly summoned witnesses and held court hearings. The family of Shen Jinguan also filed a civil lawsuit. Subsequently, the civil lawsuit was resolved through negotiation by lawyers. The verdict for the murder and other parts was announced on the 2nd. The main points were: Sun Changgen, Shu Yunfei, Chen Dequan, Zhang Zhihuo, and Yu Shentang were found guilty of homicide due to excessive defense and were each sentenced to two years of imprisonment with a five-year suspended sentence. Wang Xueling, Pan Laoqiao, and Jiangbei Xiao Si were found guilty of openly gathering a crowd to use violence and threats against public officials and were each sentenced to six months of imprisonment with a three-year suspended sentence. The number of days of detention before the final judgment was to be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Pan Laoqiao was found not guilty of destruction. Qian Wenbin was found guilty of encroaching on items held in official capacity and was sentenced to six months of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the final judgment was to be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. The trial procedure for Zhou Achang was suspended.

Page 13

Local News

Various Industries Call for Relief After the Implementation of New Import Tariffs 124

Lower New Taxes Create Dumping Opportunities for Japanese Goods

Unable to Compete, Request Reversal of Order

The new customs import tariffs have been announced by the Jianghai Customs Supervision Office and the Tax Department, and have been implemented since yesterday. These new taxes slightly reduce tariffs on cotton cloth, paper, seafood, etc. Various industries held meetings to request the government to reverse the order in order to maintain domestic industries and avoid the dumping of foreign goods. A reporter from Xinsheng News Agency specially visited the paper industry and cotton textile leaders, Jin Runyang, Zhu Wenqi, etc., yesterday to record the details as follows.

Paper Industry: Most paper imports come from Japan. Since the founding of the Republic, imports have increased year by year. In 1928, imports were 2,030,968 dan. In 1929, imports were 2,299,735 dan. In the first half of 1932, during the period when Chinese people boycotted Japanese goods, imports were 230,252 dan. Since the increase in tariffs from May of last year, domestic paper mills have been vigorously expanding, competing with Japanese paper, relying on the government's protection and increased customs duties. For example, Minfeng, Shanghai Longzhang, and other factories have been purchasing machines for making Daolin paper. Since the new taxes were announced yesterday, the import tax on foreign paper has been reduced by approximately 30%. All paper mills have been alarmed. The Chinese Paper Mills Association, in view of the reduction in import taxes on foreign paper, for example, Lian Shi yellow-edged paper, both Japanese and domestic products, cost approximately 42 yuan per ream. However, domestic goods cannot make a profit due to competition with Japanese goods. Now, if the tax on foreign paper is reduced, Japanese paper can be reduced by 5 jiao per ream, while domestic paper will inevitably lose 5 jiao. If this continues, domestic paper mills will not be able to maintain production, and Japanese paper dumping will become more severe. Therefore, an emergency meeting was held at 11:00 AM yesterday to resolve to petition the Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, Ministry of Finance, and Ministry of Industry, requesting the reversal of the order to reduce import taxes on foreign paper.

Cotton Textile Industry: Annual imports of cotton textiles, for example, in the first half of 1933, were 3,487 from Japan and 19,555 from Hong Kong. Most of the imports from Hong Kong are Japanese goods because Chinese people were severely boycotting Japanese goods at the time, so goods were rerouted through Hong Kong. Japanese cotton textile goods are dumped in various parts of our country. When Chinese-owned yarn mills and cotton textile industries heard that the import tax was being amended, they sent representatives to Beijing to petition the Ministry of Finance and other departments, requesting that it not be reduced. Since the new taxes were announced yesterday, the Cotton Textile Industry Association has been studying and comparing the new and old tariffs and will decide on a plan. However, the fabric mill parts of Chinese-owned yarn mills, such as Shenxin No. 1 Mill, Wing On Yarn Mill, Dafeng Yarn Mill, Hongzhang Yarn Mill, Hengfeng Yarn Mill, etc., have reduced labor and opened regular day shifts, taking turns to work with the original workers, due to the dumping of Japanese cloth and low market prices. Now that the import tax has been reduced, Japanese goods dumping will inevitably become more severe, and prices can be further reduced. Domestic cotton cloth will not be able to compete with them. Moreover, the raw material for cotton textiles, cotton, has increased the import tax. Therefore, it is expected that the reduction in labor in each fabric mill will inevitably increase.

German Consul General in Shanghai Issues a Written Statement 129

Declaring the Truth of the German Incident

Is Merely a Purge Movement by the National Socialist Party

According to the Central News Agency, the recent turmoil in Germany has been settled by Premier Hitler with lightning speed. German Consul General in Shanghai, Kriebel, fearing that the distance between China and Germany would lead to a lack of understanding of the incident, issued a written statement yesterday afternoon, saying that the Chinese newspapers in Shanghai have made many comments on the situation in Germany and the incident that occurred recently, but some of the reasons cited are not consistent with the facts. The German incident that occurred recently is only a purge movement that is actually needed by the National Socialist Party, eliminating those who abuse their powers and harm the public for their own selfish interests. They are a very small number, and the security and order disturbed by them have been completely restored and are as peaceful as before. As for Vice-Chancellor Papen's speech, it has nothing to do with this incident, and there is no so-called reactionary act against National Socialism. The German people are now working together wholeheartedly to support their leader Hitler. Thanks to Hitler, Germany has been rescued from the greatest difficulties in politics, economy, and culture. The realization of the rescue is due to Hitler's fundamental elimination of the idea of class struggle in Germany and the replacement of it with the spirit of mutual cooperation between entrepreneurs and craftsmen for the common welfare of the country and the people. The primary effect of this reform of thought has been proven by facts, that is, Germany has more than 3 million unemployed people who have been able to work and make a living thanks to National Socialism. Given the facts, how can it be said that this is an act of oppression of the people? As for the meeting between Hitler and Mussolini, no third party participated except for the two. As the world knows, the German people not only do not feel uneasy, but also express their understanding and support for it.

Fang Shengtao's Coffin was Sealed Yesterday 130

Li Liejun Paid Tribute on Behalf of Chairman Lin

Mayor Wu Offered Condolences on Behalf of Wang and Chiang

International Trade Bureau Plans to Promote Domestic Goods in Southeast Asia 131

According to the Central News Agency, He Bingxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau, told reporters yesterday that after Minister Chen Shi returned from an inspection in Southeast Asia, he entrusted me with the responsibility of promoting the development of trade in that area. The targets of the development are our compatriots and natives in the local area, with emphasis on the latter. Because of their habits, most of our compatriots have adopted domestic products for their food and clothing needs, and the number of products that can be further promoted is limited. Therefore, it is more important to cater to the needs of the local people. However, the first competitor to be encountered in the development is Japanese goods. Because they have the assistance of the government's great power and organized promotion, they have almost taken away the market. Even in terms of rubber cloth shoes, the local tax is 3 jiao per pair, while Japanese goods are sold for only 2.9 jiao. The extent of the price cut can be seen from this. The International Trade Bureau is now contacting domestic merchants and factories in order to investigate the nature, cost, and price of their products, and to assist manufacturers in making organized promotions to compete with other goods. Although the progress is very slow, the plan is to be thorough. At the beginning of development, losses are inevitable, but it is necessary to seek a way to develop in a difficult situation. Director He further stated that to develop foreign trade, the points that must be paid attention to are: (1) standardization of production, (2) reducing costs, (3) paying attention to international market conditions, and (4) focusing on international publicity. Chinese merchants have always not paid attention to the above points. Now that they have the awareness of developing abroad, it is hoped that they will pay close attention to this.

Foreign News Report: Naval Dispute Between Japanese and French Sailors 135

The "North-China Daily News" reports receiving two letters.

Japanese Consulate Suppresses Reckless Actions of Japanese Residents

The "China Press" reports: Last night (the 2nd) at 10 PM, a dispute arose between three French sailors and one Japanese sailor for some reason, almost leading to an incident. According to the Japanese Shanghai Daily News, the three French sailors consumed eight yuan and twenty cents worth of drinks at the Tokyo Cafe on Seward Road but only wanted to pay with one five-yuan bill, leading to an argument. Subsequently, they were surrounded by Japanese people. One of the French sailors appeared to be drunk and engaged in a brawl with a Japanese sailor from a merchant ship. The Japanese sailor knocked him down with boxing techniques, and the other two French sailors went to help. However, the Japanese people also joined in to help the Japanese sailor. Fortunately, a Japanese police officer from the Municipal Council arrived at the scene to stop the fight, and the crowd dispersed, allowing the French sailors to leave. The French sailors later went to the Hongkou police station to report that they had been beaten by Japanese people, and one of them had even lost his military hat.

The "North-China Daily News" reported yesterday (the 4th) receiving two letters. One stated that Japanese residents and sailors interfering with Municipal Council police officers performing their duties had happened more than once. The Municipal Council authorities' repeated failure to stop these illegal actions was tantamount to betraying the trust given by taxpayers and ignoring their responsibility to maintain order in the concession. It was incomprehensible that the Municipal Council police officers, even when subjected to extreme hostility and even assault, did not use legitimate self-defense measures. As a taxpayer, the writer wished to know if the Municipal Council authorities could prevent the recurrence of the Zhabei Road incident or similar incidents in the future. The other letter stated briefly that both Chinese and foreign taxpayers now wanted to know how the Municipal Council and the Consular Body would maintain security and order in the Public Concession. Shameful incidents like the recent one in Hongkou could not be ignored and should be addressed with effective and practical methods to clearly define the powers and responsibilities of the Municipal Council. If they could not fulfill their responsibilities without interference from violent Japanese crowds, it would be better not to have police at all and let things take their natural course. On Thursday night, another case occurred in the Hongkou Garden. Two foreigners were sitting on a bench outside the enclosure when suddenly a Japanese man, who appeared to be of high status, fat, and with a small mustache, asked them to let him and his wife sit with them. One of the foreigners politely told him that they were waiting for two Western women to arrive. The Japanese man should have replied that he would let his wife sit for a while and give up the seat when the Western women arrived. Unexpectedly, he raised his hand and pushed the foreigner away, leading to a fight. Immediately, a Japanese mechanic wearing a blue craftsman's uniform joined in. The three fell to the ground and wrestled, but the Japanese were always dominant. Fortunately, a special patrol officer, a Japanese detective, arrived and broke them up. The Japanese mechanic was well-versed in boxing techniques and was wrapping his arm around the foreigner's neck, trying to suffocate him. If the fight had continued, a serious incident might have occurred. Looking at the cases that have occurred in recent days, the Japanese in Shanghai harbored xenophobic intentions and were trying to create incidents deliberately. The status of the Public Concession, especially the Hongkou area, should be clarified once and for all. The Municipal Council Police Department had become merely a decoration, wasting taxpayers' money. If the same type of case could not be prevented, then Chinese and foreign residents in the concession should not pay taxes. If they could not get protection, why should they pay taxes? It would be better for the foreigners to move to the Chinese districts or the French Concession. As for the Chinese, they might know how to handle themselves, and they would likely close their shops and move to other areas that are not disturbed. One thing the writer did not understand was whether the Japanese Consulate and the Japanese Residents Association were turning a deaf ear to the repeated disturbances caused by vagrant Japanese people in the concession.

The Japanese Daily News reported that since the unfortunate incident involving marines and Western police officers on the night of the 27th, the Japanese people had been extremely agitated and had acted recklessly. Furthermore, on the night of the 1st, marines had a dispute with British and Russian people, and it was the same as the previous time; unstable actions were about to occur. Fortunately, the police of the Consulate General suppressed them, and a major problem was avoided. However, in an international city, the attitude of the Empire's subjects was repeatedly subjected to such cases, and the onlookers were going beyond normal behavior, which was extremely regrettable. The police of the Consulate General, in view of the inevitable continuation of unfortunate incidents if this continued, had been working hard to find countermeasures since the first Zhabei Road incident. Until the 2nd, after the Municipal Council police cooperated in a general mobilization, ten Japanese people had been arrested and were currently under investigation. However, to prevent the recurrence of incidents, last night (the 2nd), ten Japanese patrol officers were dispatched from the Hongkou police station of the Municipal Council in front of the Marine Corps outpost. In addition, the Chief of Police, Mr. Hanari, of the Consulate General led the entire police force to Kunshan Garden to set up a special alert line. At the same time, the atmosphere inside the Consulate General Police Department was unusually tense. To prevent such problems from happening again in the future, the Japanese residents were told to respect themselves and exercise self-control so as not to create an unstable atmosphere or escalate the incident.

Wang Delin's Letter to Compatriots Within the Pass 140

Compatriots Outside the Pass Are Tragically Massacred

Strenuous Struggle Not to Forget National Hatred

Since returning to China last summer, Wang Delin, commander-in-chief of the Northeast Volunteer Army, has reorganized his old troops and led the resistance against Japan. The struggle is arduous, and his determination has not diminished. Now that the green gauze tents are rising, it is a good opportunity to recover lost territory. Yesterday, a special envoy brought a letter to compatriots within the pass, which was handed over to his newly arrived chief of staff, Jia Mingzhou, in Shanghai for publication and appealed to all sectors for assistance. The letter reads: "To newspaper offices and compatriots across the country: Since the Japanese bandits occupied our Northeast, it has been three years. Our tens of millions of compatriots are groaning and seeking help under the trampling of iron hooves. Our hundreds of thousands of volunteer soldiers are fighting hard against the stubborn enemy, and they are bleeding for the country every day. Mountains and rivers are far apart, and days and months pass. Have our compatriots within the pass forgotten? The Japanese imperialists are determined to annex our entire China. The Tanaka Memorial has long established a conspiracy, and the recent April 17 statement has exposed their ambitions even more. Like greedy boars and long snakes, they devour everything. Looking at their recent tricks and opportunities, they are suddenly approaching North China and plotting South China. Their greedy and violent intentions are obvious. Delin is indignant at the rampant violence of the bandits and follows the military's natural duty to defend the country. After the September 18 Incident, he immediately revolted in eastern Jilin and led starving and exhausted troops to fight the stubborn enemy. They advanced wave upon wave, making repeated efforts, destroying railways, cutting off their lifeline, and conquering famous cities, establishing a foundation for our advance. Eventually, he had to retreat to Russia due to running out of ammunition and reinforcements. However, Delin's determination to resist Japan is unwavering. Since returning to China last summer, he has reorganized his old troops and continued to work, using surprise attacks and sometimes making a feint to the east while attacking in the west. Although he has not been able to recover the territory or eliminate the villains, it is enough to avenge the country's hatred and give them a lesson. In the past year, the various units have fought hundreds of battles against the enemy in Hulin, Dongning, Dunhua, Mishan, Wangqing, Yanji, Antu, Zhuhe, Binzhou, and other counties. In the end, due to a lack of pay and ammunition, the overall plan could not be carried out. I am very sad. Now that the strong bandits have entered the hall and room, the country is still singing and dancing, completely forgetting that the ownership of 2.4 million square miles of territory and 40 million compatriots has been transferred to slaves. The morale of the people is so depressed. This is indeed a tearful cry for the future of the nation. In addition, Japanese armed immigrants have recently moved to the Northeast, forcibly collecting civilian guns and confiscating civilian property, making it impossible for our compatriots to survive. Our compatriots could not bear it and rose up in resistance. Therefore, there was the case of the Yilan leader Duan, who killed his family and revolted, and the battle of Xie Wendong of Tulong Mountain, who defeated and killed Commander Iizuka. Such things are too numerous to mention. The strong bandits were angry and sent out large teams to massacre our compatriots who had no fighting power, especially in Yilan, Boli, Hongluo, Fushun, and other counties, where the damage was the most severe, numbering no less than 50,000. The inhumanity of the Japanese can be seen here. Life is uncertain, and everyone is in danger. Therefore, compatriots from all counties have brought their old and young to join our troops, crying for protection. At this critical moment of national crisis, saving the country and seeking survival depends on promoting the morale of the people. In the past, Premier Sun Yat-sen led the National Revolution and always took awakening the people as the first priority. His legacy is always the model for the world. Delin is just a soldier with a heart full of enthusiasm and loyalty, and he only wants to serve the country. He knows that starving and exhausted soldiers cannot match elite troops, and that isolated troops in the borderlands cannot match the strength of the whole country. However, he who knows that it cannot be done and still does it wants to use the righteousness of sacrificing for the country to awaken the people, inspire them to work hard, and go to the national crisis together. However, our troops have been fighting hard for many years. They have more than enough courage to kill the enemy, but the situation is becoming more and more difficult. Now that we have the right time of day, autumn and winter will arrive in a blink of an eye. The borderlands are bitterly cold, and the wind and snow are raging. Fingers and skin will be broken. Our soldiers who have no clothes or food will not die in the fierce artillery fire but will die from unbearable hunger and cold. Every time Delin thinks about this, he wanders all night, feeling sad and desperate. I still hope that our compatriots across the country will not forget the country's hatred, extend their righteous indignation, and encourage the determination to resist Japan for a long time. Do not give the impression of only having five minutes of enthusiasm. Please generously provide assistance to our troops, find ways to provide relief, so that the soldiers and horses can be full of energy, the military might can be strengthened, the shame can be washed away, the recovery of the mountains and rivers can be expected, and the revival of the nation can be relied upon. I present my words in tears, and I hope you will take care of them."

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Again Contests the Right to Manage Pilotage 141

Please Issue the Interim Regulations for Research

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce previously contested the changes to the pilotage rules promulgated by our government by a foreign customs officer, and it has sent several telegrams to the Executive Yuan to fight for this right, as reported in previous newspapers. Now it is known that the association telegraphed the government again yesterday to strive to safeguard national rights. The original text is recorded as follows: "To the Executive Yuan in Nanjing: On the first of this month, we received a letter from the Preparatory Committee of the Chinese Pilotage Association stating that, according to reliable information from foreigners, the case of our country recovering pilotage rights was previously opposed by a customs officer, who demanded amendments to the pilotage regulations promulgated on September 13 of the previous year. The Executive Yuan has acceded to the request and has four principles for the Ministry of Finance to follow in drafting the amendments. It has secretly sought the opinions of foreign customs officers and, with their approval, it can be published, named the 'Interim Regulations,' etc. According to this new chapter, seeking the opinions of foreigners first is considered non-negotiation. The power of the Customs Office is in control of financial power, and the tail is too big to shake. It is an open secret. Therefore, the content of the new chapter is not known. Our association has informed the National Government of the advantages and disadvantages and exposed the inside story. We requested the authorities to preside over the case before approving it, and to issue it to our association for discussion with relevant pilotage groups to respect public opinion. The Customs Office is employed by our country and follows the orders of the competent authorities to handle customs affairs. It does not have the right to participate in the prior formulation of central laws and regulations. If the amendment of the regulations requires its approval, it is as if the foreign customs officer who is carrying out the orders has the power of final approval. It is truly like the ancients said, 'Putting shoes and hats upside down.' If this end is opened, how can it be a country? In addition, the Customs Office is actually holding both ends and wantonly obstructing the recovery of pilotage management rights. If the amendment of the regulations is approved by it, it cannot be beneficial to our country if it is beneficial to foreigners. The advantages and disadvantages are obvious. Since the occurrence of this case, the affiliated association has appealed three times, hoping to do its best to recover the lost rights for the country. We request your institute to regard public opinion as important and to issue the interim regulations to the relevant groups for research to avoid hasty publication and further regret. It is a public convenience. Sincerely, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce."

The Test Drive Resulted in Good Results

And Will Depart on a Long-Distance Flight

The Moss steel-boned trainer plane made by the Naval Aircraft Manufacturing Department conducted a test run at Gaochang Temple Airport at 10 o'clock yesterday morning. The results were good. It will be transported to Longhua Airport within days for a sky test flight. After carefully inspecting the fuselage again, and after approval by the Naval Department, it will depart on a long-distance flight. The Dagong News Agency reporter will record the situation separately as follows.

The Fuselage Has a Fine Steel-Bone Structure 143

The self-made Moss trainer plane is a twin-folding wing amphibious type. The fuselage is entirely made of pure steel bones. It is 20 feet long. The fuselage is painted with lightweight steel zinc in the Navy's silver-gray logo. There are two seats in the front and rear for starting the car and reconnaissance. It is equipped with a 120-horsepower engine. It travels at more than 100 kilometers per hour. The load is 766 kilograms. The entire structure of the aircraft is quite exquisite, beautiful, and durable.

The Project Was Completed and Test-Driven Yesterday Morning 144

The Naval Aircraft Manufacturing Department specially planned to manufacture military trainer planes to train aviation talents and enrich the national defense force.

Since work began in April of this year, after two months of intensive work, it was fully completed on the 28th of last month. The fuselage is extremely strong. The office conducted a test run at Gaochang Temple Yanpu Airport at 10 o'clock yesterday morning to inspect the operation of the parts. For a time, the sound of the engine rattled, echoing throughout the wild. It went back and forth several times, lasting 40 minutes. The test drive resulted in good results. The manufacturing office, in order to seek stability again, is scheduled to transport it to Longhua Airport for another sky test flight within this week.

Scheduled to Depart on a Long-Distance Flight 145

The All-Zhejiang Association Presented a Letter to the Provincial Government Yesterday Asking to Stop Collecting Special Construction Donations 150

To Be the First Voice in Implementing the Reduction and Exemption of Land Tax Surcharges

The All-Zhejiang Association of this city specially presented to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, saying, "Zhejiang Province has always been known as the area with the heaviest land tax. The old Hangzhou, Jiaxing, and Huzhou prefectures followed the corruption of the former Qing Dynasty's southern transport and were particularly unequal burdens. In recent years, all new policies have been implemented, and there has been no dare not to give land tax surcharges, which has depleted resources. The people of Zhejiang have become more and more difficult, and they have even brewed the tragic scene of the collapse of Chen Village today. The central government has repeatedly issued clear orders that the land tax surcharge shall not exceed one time the regular tax. Recently, the National Finance Conference decided to abolish the land tax surcharges of various provinces and abolish all kinds of excessive taxes and miscellaneous taxes, and to allocate the stamp tax and tobacco and alcohol license tax, which belong to the national tax, to the provincial and local governments as compensation after the reduction and exemption of surcharges and miscellaneous taxes. This is the day when our people see the sky. Check the regular amount of land tax in Zhejiang Province, and the heaviest counties pay more than one penny per mu and less than one dou of offset money, which totals only 5.5 yuan. The current lightest county must pay more than 1.78 yuan in regular and surcharge mergers, which exceeds the regular tax of the heaviest counties two or three times. The surcharges are superimposed, which is an unprecedented creation of land tax. The military special donations collected since the 17th year of the Republic of China, later renamed special construction donations, are now allocated to the debt fund, with each tael of land tax and each shi of offset money adding one yuan each, which is especially large. According to the results of the discussion on the case of reviewing and reducing the land tax surcharge by your office, this special construction donation accounted for 55.6% of the surcharge in the first period and 30.3% in the second period, accounting for 40% to 50% of the total surcharge. There is also a special construction surcharge, which accounted for 8.3% of the surcharge in the first period and 9.1% in the second period. How much capacity do people have, and how can they be allowed to continue to bear this heavy burden superimposed? Although it is stated that this special donation is not a permanent burden and will be exempted after the debt settlement case is completely cleared, and each county is allowed to deduct it when calculating the total amount of land tax surcharge, this special donation is exempted from the calculation to show that it does not violate the central government's clear order of not exceeding one time the regular tax. However, all surcharges are temporary in nature, and it is not only the special construction donation that is the case. The burden on the people of Zhejiang is very heavy, and there is an urgent need for review and reduction. Fortunately, the central government is aware of the financial difficulties of local governments and the suffering of the people, and it is willing to allocate national taxes to subsidize the provincial and local governments. Our Zhejiang debt fund should not be worried about being unsettled. We should immediately stop collecting this special construction donation in the next period of this year. At the same time, we should strictly implement austerity policies and gradually reduce other surcharges and miscellaneous taxes to start anew with the people. Our association believes that the provincial and county finances are equally scarce, and various surcharges are related to the promotion of new policies. Therefore, we dare not request the simultaneous abolition of all the donations that harm the people, but only ask that the special construction donation, which harms the people most, be stopped first as a preliminary measure to reduce and exempt land tax surcharges in accordance with the order of the Yuan. This should not be difficult. If we can reduce the people's financial resources by one point, we will retain one point of vitality for the countryside. Your Excellency has lingering illnesses and must be able to grant our request to comfort the expectations of the people of Zhejiang. Therefore, we urgently present this matter and ask you to review and implement it.

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Rickshaw Affairs Committee, in order to confirm the owners of public rickshaws (i.e., yellow rickshaws), has now stipulated that starting next month, i.e., August, anyone applying for a public rickshaw license (commonly known as a "chao hui") must first submit the certificate of ownership issued by the committee for verification; otherwise, the license will not be issued. Abusing a Girl, Husband Unable to Dissuade Her

Drinking Kerosene and Stabbing Herself in the Head and Neck

The Injustices Suffered by Zhuang Yuanda and Others Are Cleared

Major Robbery Case: All Four Defendants Found Not Guilty Yesterday 163

On the afternoon of the 9th of last month, at the accounting firm of Xue Mai Luo at 9 Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, the comprador Zhou Jinggeng sent his employees Gao Yushu, Feng Ti'e, and Wan Guirong to the bank to exchange 18,900 yuan of new banknotes from the China Industrial Bank. They returned to the office at 4:30 PM, preparing to deliver them to Yiyuan Dog Racing Track for use that evening. Unexpectedly, armed robbers broke in, stole 12,000 yuan (6,000 yuan each) from Gao and Feng, and fled. According to Zhang's confession, they then arrested Zhuang Yuanda, the owner of a winery, Zhuang Jimeng, Wang Lianyou, a hardware peddler, and Tang Qingyue, the director of Dade Hospital on Gordon Road, who was from Taicang. The four men were transferred to the Second Special District District Court, and the police department filed a public prosecution based on Article 1, Clause 14 of the Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits. The victims, as plaintiffs, also hired lawyers to file private lawsuits, requesting the recovery of the stolen money. The case had been tried and Zhang was ordered to remain in custody, while Zhuang and Wang were each released on bail with three guarantors, and Tang Qingyue remained on his original bail, awaiting sentencing on a scheduled date, as previously reported. Yesterday was the date for the sentencing in this case. The police brought Zhang Zuming to the court at 9:00 AM. Zhuang, Wang, and Tang, who were released on bail, along with their defense lawyer Osen and Zhang Zuming's defense lawyer Lin Yingqing, arrived at the court one after another at 9:00 AM. At 10:00 AM, Judge Li Changnian attended the first criminal court, summoned the defendants to the dock, and after briefly asking each person's name, read out the main text of the judgment, saying, "Zhang Zuming, Zhuang Jimeng, Wang Lianyou, and Tang Qingyue are all not guilty. The plaintiff's incidental civil lawsuit is dismissed." After the judgment, Zhang Zuming was ordered to be transferred to the detention center during the appeal period, and the others remained on their original bail awaiting further instructions. Furthermore, in the news coverage of the trial on the 29th of last month, it was reported that Zhang Lifeng, the manager of Jing Daxiang Money Shop, testified in court about Zhang Zuming's deposit. It has now been learned that it was actually Zhang Lianfang, the manager of Heng Daxiang Hardware Store, who testified. The reporter was standing too far away at the time, and the voice was too low, leading to the misunderstanding. This correction is hereby attached.

National Product Leather Suitcases Selling Well in Southeast Asia 164

Approximately One Million Yuan Annually

Further Improvement Could Lead to Greater Development

According to a report from the Guidance Department of the International Trade Bureau, the export of domestic products to Malaya has gradually increased in recent years, with the leather suitcase industry being the most prominent. It has been found that these products come from Qingdao, Hong Kong, Guangzhou, and other places. Twenty years ago, suitcases in Malaya were all Western or Japanese goods, and domestic products had almost no foothold. In recent years, domestic leather suitcases have sold well in Southeast Asia, with an annual value of one million yuan. If they are further improved and actively promoted, Western and Japanese leather suitcases will have no room to stand.

Reasons for Inability to Manufacture in Southeast Asia 165

The manufacture of leather suitcases is a semi-handicraft industry, so places in temperate zones such as Shanghai and Guangzhou are suitable. People in temperate zones can work from 8:00 AM to 8:00 PM, for more than ten hours. Workers in tropical zones are absolutely incapable of doing this. Chinese wages are also low, so the cost is naturally lower. Therefore, manufacturing leather suitcases in Southeast Asia is not as convenient as transporting them from China.

Current Status of Domestic Leather Suitcase Sales 166

The sales of domestic leather suitcases in Southeast Asia were most prosperous in the past few years, with annual exports to Malaya valued at several million yuan. However, in recent years, due to the economic downturn, the value has only been one million yuan. However, the lives of people in general commercial ports are becoming increasingly prosperous, and they love to be modern. The old-fashioned domestic leather suitcases are gradually being replaced by the semi-handicraft Western leather suitcase industry. Therefore, the emerging domestic leather suitcase industry still has hope for development in Malaya, if there is no special reason.

Death of Promising Young Navigator Sha Huijia 167

A Major Loss of Navigational Talent

Mr. Sha Huijia, a member of the Shanghai Pilot Association and a member of the Shanghai Maritime Administration's Ship Collision Dispute Handling Committee, served in the maritime industry for more than ten years. His knowledge and experience were widely admired. Unfortunately, he suddenly passed away from typhoid fever at his residence in Shanghai at 4:00 PM on the 30th of last month, at the young age of 31. Chinese and foreign maritime circles were deeply saddened by his passing. Mr. Sha, also known as Yin Cheng, was from Jiangyin, Jiangsu. In 1921, he graduated from Wusong Fisheries School. He then worked for Chang'an Shipping Company's Hua'an Merchant Shipping, rising from second officer to first officer to captain. In the five or six years that Mr. Sha served as captain, he traveled back and forth across the North and South Pacific Oceans and never caused a single accident, nor did he cause the company or the insurance company even the slightest loss. His excellent navigational skills were praised by Chinese and foreign maritime circles. In the autumn of the year before last, he joined the Shanghai Pilot Association as a member (Chinese pilots accounted for only two of the forty pilots). He guided foreign merchant ships in and out of Shanghai Port. The major foreign shipping companies

Photograph of Sha Huijia 168

expressed their admiration for his knowledge and skills. After the establishment of the Shanghai Maritime Administration's Ship Collision Dispute Handling Committee, he was hired as a committee member. The companies were particularly impressed with his mediation and adjudication of ship collision cases. Mr. Sha was in the prime of his life when he suddenly passed away. China's maritime community already lamented the scarcity of talent, and now they have suffered this major loss. The mourners are not only those in the maritime community.

A Young Man Commits Suicide in a Hotel in Xiaodongmen 169

Four Letters Left for Various People

Forced to Commit Suicide, But Not Willing

At around 11:00 PM the night before last, a young male customer arrived at the Central Hotel in Xiaodongmen, claiming to be Ding Senfu, 23 years old, from Pudong. He paid one yuan for the room and then went out for a drink, asking the bellboy Wang Bingrong to lock the room. He returned to his room to rest at around 12:00 PM. Unexpectedly, the customer had not gotten up by yesterday afternoon. As usual, the bellboy asked the guest if he wanted to extend his stay. However, there was no response after knocking on the door for a long time. The bellboy knew something was wrong and reported it to the accountant, who devised a way to pry open the door. Suddenly, they saw the guest lying on the bed, foaming at the mouth, his face pale. He was barely breathing, and they knew he had taken poison. An empty bottle of A.O. was found on the table. According to those who recognized it, it was a sleeping pill. The incident was immediately reported to the Second Precinct of the First District for investigation. Chief Liu immediately dispatched Police Officer Li Fuyi to investigate. At the same time, the poisoned man was taken to Shanghai Hospital for treatment, but his life was hanging by a thread. Police Officer Li also found four letters left by the poisoned man: (1) to his sister Ding Jiazhen at 13 Jiangjiayuan, Xiaguan, Nanjing, (2) to his uncle Ding Zhuanghui at 25 Jinyuli, Nan Zhujiaqiao, and two other letters to relatives and friends. The letters stated the reason for his suicide, saying that he was forced to repay debts by the owner of a certain cigarette paper shop and the shareholder Yue Jinhe. Because he had been unemployed for a long time, he had no money to repay the debts. Unexpectedly, they threatened to use a gun against him, so he preferred to commit suicide. However, he was not willing, but was forced. He asked his uncle to seek justice, etc.
