The Sanitary Authorities are Intensifying Care Due to the Prevalence of Heat and Epidemics 173

Hospitals for Epidemic Diseases are Striving to Provide Treatment

There is Great Panic Over Drinking Water in the Interior

The weather in Shanghai is extremely hot, and this has been the case for ten days. The daily high temperature has always reached 102-103 degrees. The city's health authorities are doing everything possible to prevent and treat epidemics, and the hospitals for epidemic diseases are also intensifying their work. Fortunately, true cholera has not yet been discovered, but the drought and lack of rain have also made drinking water a problem in the interior. The reporter from Shen Shi News Agency explored and recorded the situation as follows:

Intensifying Epidemic Prevention and Free Injections 174

In view of the extremely hot weather and the proliferation of epidemics, the Municipal Health Bureau is paying special attention to prevention work. The Nanshi Clinic, the Municipal

Hospital for Epidemic Diseases, and the City Center Clinic are all administering preventative injections at the same time. More than 10,000 citizens have received injections. The bureau is paying particular attention to organizations. The bureau has sent personnel to various schools in the city to administer injections. The number of people injected so far: Cao Nan Elementary School 300 people, Anbang Elementary School 61 people, Pengpu Elementary School 372 people, Huadong Elementary School 740 people, Jieyuan Elementary School 84 people, Tan Zhen Elementary School 198 people, Xiaozha Elementary School 83 people, Yangcun Elementary School 150 people, McLaren High School 165 people, Yingsi Elementary School 300 people, Fahua Elementary School 155 people, Pingan Elementary School 221 people, Bengbu Elementary School 340 people, Guanghua University 408 people, a total of 3,417 people. In addition, 118 people have been injected at Yizhong Machinery Company.

Hospitals are Working Under Great Strain 175

The epidemic hospitals in the city are all intensifying their work during this epidemic. The Shanghai Epidemic Hospital on Xizang Road has treated more than 2,000 people since it began treating patients on the 25th of last month. The most common cases are heatstroke, malaria, and gastroenteritis. The Hongkou Epidemic Hospital on Tangshan Road opened on the first day of this month and has treated more than 1,000 people in the past three days. The Special District Rickshaw Association, in order to protect the health of the coolies, has set up five free clinics and has arranged for Minqiang Hospital on Robert Dollar Road to provide free preventative injections for the coolies. In addition, the Red Cross Epidemic Hospital will be opening earlier from today to benefit the citizens. The health departments of the Public Concession and the French Concession are also administering injections to residents and posting slogans on the streets, advising residents to pay attention to their diet to prevent cholera.

Crop and Pond Dryness: Disaster Already Formed 176

The weather is severely dry, and rural areas are suffering from disasters. This has become an unavoidable fact. According to farmers who have recently come to Shanghai from the countryside, there has been no rain for a long time in the villages, and farmers are relying on waterwheels for irrigation. However, this is a drop in the bucket and does not help the situation. Moreover, the water stored in fields and ponds is almost completely dry. This year's autumn harvest will be at most 50% for low-lying fields, and high-lying fields will likely yield nothing. Although there have been occasional bumper harvests followed by disasters in recent years, farmers, while not wealthy enough to accumulate savings, have been able to barely maintain their lives. This year's drought, once it takes hold, will plunge rural areas into dire straits.

Panic Over Drinking Water Among Villagers 177

The drinking water problem caused by the severe drought is also quite serious. In cities, people are not aware of the problem because of the supply from waterworks. However, in the countryside, where people rely on rivers, the long drought and lack of rain have caused rivers to dry up, creating a serious problem. In places such as Suzhou, Wuxi, Hangzhou, and Jiaxing, river channels are shallow and silted, and the water quality is turbid. Residents are feeling a severe lack of drinking water. If there is no more rain, a major panic is bound to ensue.

Xu Zhou Bandit Zhang Huaiqing Extorts 200,000 from Ji Juemi

Ji Sends People Twice to Wuxi to Negotiate, Agreeing to Pay 4,000 Yuan

Luring Him to Shanghai to Collect the Money, Reporting to the Police to Arrest Him

丨Ji's Ancestral Graves Have Been Dug Up and Destroyed by Bandits丨

Ji Juemi, the manager of Arnhold, Karberg & Co. on Nanjing Road and a native of Xuzhou, received five threatening letters from bandits between November last year and the 10th of last month, demanding 200,000 yuan, or else they would use bombs and guns. Ji knew that this was the work of a notorious local bandit, so he secretly requested the Xuzhou Garrison Command to arrest and pursue him, but no clues could be found. Recently, it was discovered that the bandit leader, Zhang Huaiqing, a 32-year-old native of Xuzhou, was using the alias Gu Xinzhai and staying in Wuxi. On the 21st of last month, Ji sent his representative, Pan Litian, to Wuxi to find him. Pan met Zhang at the Railway Hotel, and after negotiations, the amount was reduced by 80,000 yuan. Pan only agreed to several thousand yuan and returned unsatisfied. On the 26th, he sent his cook, Zhu Benqing, to Wuxi to negotiate again. As a result, they agreed on 4,000 yuan, instructing him to come to Shanghai to collect the money, assuring him that nothing else would happen. Until the day before yesterday, they tricked him into coming to Shanghai and temporarily staying in an empty house at 1255 Avenue Foch (note: this house is owned by Arnhold, Karberg & Co.). It was agreed that 2,000 yuan would be paid first. Around 10 o'clock, they secretly informed the Yangshupu Police Station, and Chinese Detective Liu Wenhan, together with a Western detective, accompanied Zhu Benqing with hell money from the Bank of the Underworld, using two real ten-yuan notes from the China Industrial Bank and the China Commercial Bank on top to make it look like 2,000 yuan. Zhu went in first, and just as he was handing over the money, the Chinese and Western detectives rushed in and arrested him. Inside the house, there was already an opium pipe, an opium lamp, and an opium tool, which were all taken to the police station and confiscated. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Special District Court.

In the Third Criminal Court, the Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer, Li Zhishan, described the events, stating that an investigation revealed that the victim in this case, Ji Juemi, was originally named Pan when he was young in Xuzhou. He changed his name to Ji after coming to Shanghai. Therefore, his ancestral graves were all in his hometown. Unexpectedly, in November of last year, the bandits dug up his ancestral graves, took away the remains, and hid them without a trace. Later, they sent a letter stating that if he wanted to retrieve the remains, he would have to pay 200,000 yuan, or else they would burn the bones to ashes and continue to dig up the remains of his parents, and then use bombs and guns to harm him. The victim knew that this was the work of local bandits, so he reported it to the local garrison command for arrest. The garrison command sent troops to suppress the bandits, causing the defendant to have no place to stand. Recently, he fled to Wuxi, and there was also a public notice for his arrest. Now, the police station requests an extension for further investigation. The evidence, including the hell money and a travel schedule from Wuxi to Shanghai found on his person, as well as the threatening letters and public notices, were presented for inspection. The defendant confessed that he had recently come to Shanghai from his hometown to sell cloth, had not been to Wuxi, and had nothing to do with the grave digging and extortion. He also denied having contacted Pan Litian and Zhu Benqing. He claimed his name was Gu Xinzhai, not Zhang Huaiqing, and his other statements were evasive, asking for leniency. The victim, Ji Juemi, was not present, but Pan and Zhu testified about the events. Zhu stated that he had previously had a dispute over selling livestock in his hometown, and the defendant had robbed him of all his money and then kidnapped him and demanded ransom. Because he had no money to pay, he was released. Zhu claimed that Zhang was a notorious bandit leader. Judge Liu Yugui ordered that he be remanded in custody and rescheduled the hearing.

Villagers in Shanghai West Side Initiate a Prayer for Rain 181

Since the beginning of summer, the weather has been hot and there has been no rainfall. The cotton and bean seedlings planted by farmers are withering, and the rice paddies are dry, showing signs of drought. Therefore, farmers in the Longhua, Hongqiao, and Fahua areas of Shanghai West Side have initiated a prayer for rain starting yesterday. Beforehand, they contacted various villages to beat gongs and inform the public to offer sacrifices to the gods and pray for rain, parading back and forth. The various sub-stations 123 of the Sixth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, fearing a large crowd, specially dispatched regular shift police officers to accompany them. Although the matter is absurd, it is driven by utter sincerity.

Dispute Over Setting Up a Watermelon Stall: Child Pushed Down, Falls Ill, and Dies 182

A hawker named Zhang Liangtai recently set up a watermelon stall on Rue Eugène Bard in Hongkou to take advantage of the summer season. His stall was in front of the rice shop opened by Liu Rongchang. The watermelon rinds were scattered all over the place, so Liu negotiated with him about the land rental fee, and a quarrel ensued. At that time, Zhang's elderly mother was standing by, holding her three-year-old grandson, watching idly. Seeing this, she stepped forward to intervene, and Liu pushed her, causing both the old woman and the baby to fall to the ground. After returning home, the child had chills and fever that night, and the child died the next day. Zhang claimed that Liu pushed his mother, causing his son to fall down and die unjustly, and requested an investigation. The Third Sub-station of the Fifth District instructed the local security officer to report the case to the court for an autopsy yesterday.

Fan Zhixuan's Personal Fan Painting Exhibition 184

He further became a student of the famous Sichuan painters Zhang Shanzi and Daqian, devoting himself to the Shigu, Qingxiang Laoren, and Qushan schools. Even small paintings on silk or paper are considered precious. Recently, at the Dafengtang Painting and Calligraphy Exhibition, many of his paintings were sold, demonstrating his artistic skill and the large number of people who appreciate his work. Now, he is exhibiting over two hundred fan paintings created over the years at his personal fan painting exhibition held at the Tonghui Elementary School on Rue Wagner in the French Concession on July 4th, 5th, and 6th. The painting shown here is one of his exhibited works, with rich ink colors and a peaceful charm reminiscent of Fengchang. It is also said that to broaden his circle of artistic connections, each fan painting is only sold for two or four yuan.

Letter 194

To the Editor,

We were shocked to read the large headline in your newspaper on the 2nd of this month, "Descendants of Jiang Mule Dispute Property in Lawsuit." The lawsuit between Jiang Jingfen and Jiang Yang relates to a separate matter. As for involving our family's origins, your newspaper, long a leader in domestic news, should record information accurately. We do not know the basis of this interview. Our ancestors founded the family with their bare hands and managed it diligently. The neighborhood knows this well and regards us as a model family. In particular, on September 18th of the 18th year of the Republic [1929], the Shen Bao published an article after the manuscript of "Old Man Yao's Collection of Unofficial History of Hong and Yang" in Banqiao, which is enough to demonstrate the facts and public opinion. Now, your newspaper has insulted our ancestors with groundless facts, causing shame to future generations. We are writing to request that your newspaper publish and correct our letter, and express your apologies to our family. We hope you will consider this. Sincerely, Jiang Xijue, representative of the Jiang Chunhui Tang family, July 3, 23rd year of the Republic [1934].

Acknowledgment: We received a copy of the Bank Weekly, No. 856, courtesy of the Bank Weekly Society. Thank you.

Special Item

Shanghai Municipal Public Bond Regulations (4) 195

Passed by the Legislative Yuan on June 29th

Agreement and Attachments: On May 10, 23rd year of the Republic (1934 AD), the Shanghai Municipal Government (hereinafter referred to as the "Municipal Government"), represented by Mayor Wu Tiecheng, and Sin Feng & Co. (hereinafter referred to as the "Company") signed this agreement in Shanghai. The Municipal Government, in order to raise funds for improving roads and bridges in Zhabei, constructing a sports field, museum, library, hospital, slaughterhouse, and developing other undertakings in the city center, was approved to issue a 12-year, 7% public bond with a total amount of 3.5 million Chinese silver dollars, named the Shanghai Municipal Public Bond of the 23rd year of the Republic. The Municipal Government wishes to entrust the Company to organize and be responsible for a syndicate, with the Company leading the syndicate to underwrite this public bond. The Company is willing to organize this syndicate in accordance with the following terms. With mutual consent, based on the above circumstances, the Municipal Government hereby entrusts the Company to organize and be responsible for a syndicate (hereinafter referred to as the "Syndicate") to underwrite the Shanghai Municipal Public Bond of the 23rd year of the Republic, and the Company is willing to accept the Municipal Government's entrustment in accordance with the following terms, without withdrawal.

Article 1: The Municipal Government shall submit a copy of the National Government's document approving the issuance of this public bond to the Company for reference. The National Government shall, in accordance with the general situation at the time, allow this public bond to be exempt from any taxes. The bond certificates of this public bond shall state all the terms and conditions and have attached interest coupons. The form of the bond and interest coupons can be found in "Attachment A."

Article 2: The Syndicate shall be responsible for underwriting the entire amount of this public bond at 93% of its face value in silver.

Article 3: The Municipal Government shall allow the use of drawn bond certificates and matured interest coupons of this public bond for the payment of taxes.

Article 4: The Municipal Government shall establish a supervisory committee (hereinafter referred to as the "Committee") to supervise the use of the actual proceeds of this public bond. The Committee shall consist of seven persons residing in Shanghai, who shall exercise their supervisory powers in accordance with these terms. The Municipal Government shall be responsible for establishing and maintaining the Committee. The Committee members shall be the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, the Director of the Public Works Bureau, the Director of the Education Bureau, the Chairman of the National Debt Fund Management Committee, one representative from the Municipal Provisional Council, one representative from the Shanghai Bankers Association, and one representative from the Company, with the Director of the Finance Bureau serving as Chairman.

Article 5: The Municipal Government shall reserve a portion of the actual proceeds of this public bond, totaling 555,000 silver dollars, approximately equal to one year's principal and interest repayment. The remaining funds shall be used for handling and improving the aforementioned public undertakings.

Article 6: The Municipal Government shall provide an absolute guarantee for this public bond and shall designate all license fees from automobiles, motorcycles, bicycles, and pedicabs as the priority fund for repaying the principal and interest. This income shall continue to be given priority until the principal and interest of this public bond and other related future loans are paid off. The Municipal Government shall deposit these license fees with the National Debt Fund Management Committee as soon as they are received, and credit them to the account of this public bond. The committee shall execute the repayment of principal and interest and directly pay the holders of matured interest coupons and drawn bond certificates in accordance with the principal and interest repayment schedule contained in this public bond.

Article 7: To further increase the guarantee, if the license fees for automobiles, motorcycles, bicycles, and pedicabs are insufficient to cover the principal and interest of this public bond at any time, the Municipal Government shall give priority to the license fees from various rickshaws, freight carts, and other vehicles. If the repayment of principal and interest of this public bond urgently requires the license fees from the following items, the Municipal Government is willing to deposit these fees with the National Debt Fund Management Committee at any time and credit them to the fund account of this public bond.

Article 8: If the various license fees for automobiles, motorcycles, bicycles, pedicabs, rickshaws, freight carts, and other vehicles collected by the Municipal Government are insufficient to cover the repayment of principal and interest of this public bond, the Municipal Government shall be responsible for allocating other non-guaranteed income in advance to make up the shortfall.

Article 9: During the validity of this agreement, the Committee or the Company may, at any time, have one auditor appointed by the National Debt Fund Management Committee and one auditor appointed by the Company audit the accounts related to this agreement at the Municipal Government, and the Municipal Government shall pay a reasonable handling fee.

Article 10: To facilitate the handling of this public bond by the National Debt Fund Management Committee and to protect the bondholders, the National Debt Fund Management Committee may send one or more representatives to be stationed at the various agencies of the Municipal Government that collect the aforementioned license fees and authorize the representatives to collect these license fees and deliver them to the committee to be credited to the account of this public bond. If the committee does not send representatives, the Municipal Government shall transfer all of these license fees to the committee for accounting when they are received. If the amount received exceeds the fixed principal and interest fund of this public bond, it shall be returned to the Municipal Government immediately. (To be continued)

Reading Q&A

Subjective Truth and Objective Truth丨Answer to Mr. Meitang丨 196

In terms of literal meaning, subjective truth refers to truth that can only exist in the human mind and not in external things. Conversely, objective truth refers to truth that exists in the objective world (i.e., external things) and cannot exist in human thought. Therefore, when talking about subjective truth, it is tantamount to saying, "What I think is how it is," while objective truth is saying, "I cannot participate with my opinion, it only depends on what the facts are."

However, in fact, such truth cannot be established. "What I think is how it is," and you also think is how it is, then everyone can call a deer a horse, how can this be considered truth? Truth must be distinguished from falsehood. If everyone uses themselves as the standard, it will be impossible to distinguish who is true and who is false. This kind of subjective truth cannot be considered truth. Objective truth is the same. If objective truth only exists in external things and not in human thought, then there is no way for human thought to relate to objective truth. Objective truth cannot be recognized by humans. If humans cannot recognize it, how can they know that it is truth?

Therefore, subjective truth and objective truth are two opposing things, but if the two things are distinctly separated and seen only as the dead literal definitions, then both will not be established. How can we make both of them established? That is to grasp the unity of these opposites.

How to grasp the unity of the opposites of subjective and objective? Before explaining, let's use an old story as an example: Somewhere there was a shield hanging, and two people came to judge it. One person stood in front of the shield and saw that it was gold, and insisted that the shield was gold. The other person stood behind the shield and saw that it was red, and insisted that the shield was red. So the two quarreled. In fact, the color of the shield was different on both sides. Each of them saw one side and did not see the other side. If they had seen both sides, they would not have quarreled.

The two people mentioned here both held a subjective truth. This kind of subjective truth is not the subjective opinion purely created by arbitrary delusion mentioned earlier, but because the observation is incomplete, causing people to hold onto one side of the thing, resulting in a one-sided truth. Although this truth is incomplete, it does grasp one side of the objective thing, so it can still be regarded as truth. At the same time, this truth is only one side of what the observer subjectively sees and cannot represent the true objective thing, so it is always subjective truth. Only when both sides of the shield have been observed and the opinions of the two people are combined can it become objective truth.

Therefore, subjective truth is one side of objective truth, and it is incomplete objective truth. When we find objective truth, we can overthrow subjective truth, but we cannot therefore completely reject the value of subjective truth. Because external things are multifaceted, our ability to recognize things cannot immediately grasp all aspects of things. Our recognition of things gradually deepens one aspect at a time, and our knowledge gradually increases. To achieve objective truth, we must first go through the process of subjective truth, starting from a partial, incomplete knowledge, and gradually reaching the realm of completeness. That is to say: "In any subjective truth, there will inevitably be a seed of objective truth. The increase of subjective truth is the growth of this seed. When it grows to a certain limit, the seed becomes a true objective truth." This is the so-called development of the process. People who do not understand this principle think that subjective truth and objective truth are absolutely separated and cannot be transformed into each other. This kind of view that separates things is the so-called metaphysical view. Its unreasonableness was mentioned earlier.

Another point to note is that the properties of the various aspects of external things are not necessarily like a shield that can be placed there for us to see. Water is a fluid and transparent, which can be known at a glance, but the property that it will boil at a temperature of 100 degrees is not known at a glance. To know that it will boil, it must be burned on a fire. The properties of all things, as long as they are slightly deeper, must be processed and transformed by people before they can be revealed. That is to say, if people want to know the properties of things, they must practice in the things. The more practice, the deeper the knowledge of things. Each practice provides us with one aspect of the truth of things, and the sum of the truths of various practices can form the complete objective truth.

We cannot ignore subjective truth, but we must not exaggerate subjective truth. Subjective truth contains the seed of objective truth, so it cannot be ignored, but it is only a seed, so it cannot be exaggerated. We must constantly practice and constantly transform things to increase our knowledge. One of the characteristics of idealistic philosophy is that it separates us from practice and closes us in the subjective ivory tower of concepts, and we cannot deeply create in layers towards the internal properties of things, so we must oppose idealism. (The End)

Spring and Autumn

The Fragrant and Elusive Record of Imperial Cuisine 197

—Original by Princess Der Ling of Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

Among the various seafood items, the commonly used ones include shark fin, fish maw, fish tripe, bird's nest, sea cucumber, etc. Their various methods of preparation are roughly the same as those outside the palace, so there is no need to repeat them.

Generally, the price of each kind of seafood is always a few points higher than ordinary beef, mutton, chicken, and duck, presumably because it is more difficult to obtain. However, in terms of their true taste, I really dare not compliment them. Even the Empress Dowager looks at various seafood dishes very plainly; she especially dislikes sea cucumber. Sea cucumber is a bland and tasteless thing, and its shape is even more ugly, but people generally say that it has nourishing properties, so it has to be included among those real delicacies.

The Empress Dowager also has a particularly favorite dish, which is Qingdun Duck Tongues. These duck tongues are stewed together with duck meat, with at least twenty or thirty of them floating on top of the soup. Because this is the Empress Dowager's favorite dish, it is always served in a specially prepared apricot-yellow bowl, and it is always placed closest to the Empress Dowager. In addition, there is also a kind of salted duck webs, which is an essential special dish for every "snack"; but this thing has only one layer of webbed skin that can be chewed on, and the rest is all bones. Duck gizzards, duck organs, etc., are also often prepared in various different ways to serve as the Empress Dowager's side dishes. From these few points, it can be seen that the Empress Dowager is particularly fond of ducks; except for that piece of smelly duck butt, she simply refuses to let it go easily.

In the summer, various melons and fruits are on the market, and the chefs in the imperial kitchen have to use them to make several fresh seasonal special dishes to offer to the Empress Dowager as a tribute. Among them, one that the Empress Dowager appreciates the most is "Watermelon Boat." Its method of preparation is to dig out all the pulp from the watermelon, and fill it with diced chicken, diced ham, fresh lotus seeds, longan, walnuts, pine nuts, almonds, etc., and cover it again, and simmer it over low heat through water for several hours. The pure and delicious taste is not difficult for us to imagine! (74)

Mahjong 198

— Wang Shouqiu

In China, there is nothing else to boast about, except that mahjong tiles, numbering one hundred and thirty-six, can actually cross the Eastern Sea and become popular in Europe and America. Isn't that something to be proud of? Originally, mahjong is a national treasure of China. Among the 450 million men and women compatriots in China, at least 300 million can play. I often say: Everyone says that education in China is not widespread enough, so most are illiterate, but this is a mistake. If they can't read, how can they recognize the East, South, West, North, Middle, Prosperity, Dragon, Phoenix, and the one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, eight, nine of ten thousands on the mahjong tiles?

Among the important figures of the party-state, there are also many who are addicted to this game, and their bamboo combat techniques are also very exquisite. Especially a certain general who once dominated the two lakes, his mahjong skills can be called the best among the important figures of the party-state!

Apart from gambling, mahjong seems to have no other use, but the explanation of the XX department is that mahjong itself cannot be regarded as a prohibited item and can be transported without obstruction. This wonderful explanation is truly only known to heaven. We common people are really unfathomable and dare not guess! I have a friend who can look at mahjong with his eyes closed. He only needs to touch it with two fingers, as if he can see it. Moreover, he can look at all thirteen tiles upside down from beginning to end. This can indeed be said to be the Mahjong King!

By the Wusong River 199

— Jing Renfang

"Hang yu! Hang yu..." A group of shirtless coolies are carrying goods that have just been transported from somewhere to the warehouse, constantly coming and going, going and coming again. The sweat on their bodies gushes out like the tide, and their mouths are constantly roaring in a miserable tone. For the sake of life, they have to work so hard. The water in the Wusong River, black in color, is hysterically surging. It is evaporated by the intense sunlight, and stirred by the breeze. A very fishy and foul odor quickly invades everyone's nostrils. It is awfully unpleasant....

Two or three Jiangbei children, with two terribly thin legs bare, shirtless, are digging here and there in the filthy mud by the riverbank, hoping to get something without cost. After a while, one child picks up a broken bowl, and another child picks up a silver coin. The child who picks up the silver coin continues to dig with a triumphant smile. The child who picks up the broken bowl is crying, but he is still working hard, hoping to pick up something more valuable than a silver coin. People's hearts are the fiercest, especially the hearts of poor people.

The boatman who shakes the boat is desperately holding the long oar with force, turning left and right as he shakes it, singing various vulgar and obscene mountain songs in his mouth, while smiling. The songs they sing do not have the bravery or sadness of the Song of the Volga Boatmen. The evening glow in the sky is presented in the boundless clouds, with red and yellow, how bright and beautiful, but soon, you will be invaded by the black devil and destroy your body. The water in the Wusong River is hysterically surging.

Stinking for Ten Thousand Years 200

— Feng Momin

Yesterday I passed a door on the road, and the white curtains of filial piety showed that someone must have died, but there was only a middle-aged woman crying in the curtains, and the rest were making noise at the door, and they were all pinching their noses and shaking their heads. Perhaps it was the hot weather and the corpse was stinking, which is also a very normal thing, but the others were discussing it, saying that this person had fallen to his death in a latrine, so the stench was overflowing, even after washing, the stench was not gone.

It is said that this person was very good and very honest during his lifetime. He moved from Jiangbei to Jiangnan more than ten years ago and never quarreled with anyone, so the neighbors nearby praised him. One day, he suddenly did not return all night. It was thought that he was socializing at a friend's house, but unexpectedly, a dead person was found in the latrine at the entrance of the alley. The crowd went to watch and found that it was the middle-aged woman's husband, so sadness came from it.

"Stinking for ten thousand years" and "becoming famous for hundreds of generations" are two sentences, one is cursing people, and the other is flattering people. If someone is a great traitor and cunning, doing all kinds of evil, they should be stinking for ten thousand years. If someone has a pure heart, they are cursed for stinking for ten thousand years, but those treacherous people are flattered with becoming famous for hundreds of generations. It is really confusing, no wonder the society is getting darker and darker.

The person who fell and died in the latrine, although the appearance is unbearably stinking, the heart is very pure. Rather than praising Zhang San and Li Si for becoming famous for hundreds of generations, it is better to praise the person in the latrine. Black and white can still be distinguished, but they spent money to buy the praises of becoming famous for hundreds of generations, but in fact they will be stinking for tens of thousands of years.

General Mobilization of Laughter

Acute Mistakes 203

— Zhan Lu

The weather is extremely hot, and people's hearts are also becoming irritable. When encountering an impetuous person, the heat above ninety degrees makes their heart feel like it's on fire, unbearably impatient. If an impetuous person encounters a slow-paced person, they often show a reckless expression before the other person finishes speaking, leading to many jokes. I've recorded some of them...

Mr. Zhang saw his tenant farmer being escorted into the city by the police, with iron chains clanking, which was quite pitiful. Mr. Zhang said, "Amu Lin, what crime have you committed?" The tenant farmer said, "I committed theft." "Amu Lin, that's not good. What did you steal from someone?" "Sir, I didn't steal anything, I only picked up a piece of straw rope." Mr. Zhang angrily said, "The current criminal law is too harsh. You only picked up a piece of straw rope, and they shouldn't be escorting you into the city like they're capturing a major thief." The tenant farmer said, "I haven't finished speaking. I only picked up a piece of straw rope, and the rope was tied to someone's cow. So I led it to my own home."

A young man dragged an old man to the court to file a complaint, saying that the old man scolded him loudly, bordering on insult, so he sued him. The official asked the old man, "What authority do you have to scold a young man? What kind of person are you?" The old man slowly replied, "I am a country person." The official angrily said, "So you are a country bumpkin! You are not related to the young man, so how can you insult him?" The old man said, "Don't be angry, Your Honor, let me finish my explanation. I am a country person and don't recognize hunchbacks, calling them 'swollen backs.' It is natural for elders to instruct juniors, and it shouldn't be considered an insult."

In an era of "national extravagance showing frugality," adults and gentlemen often dress like old country people. If you "only judge people by their clothes," it's easy to make a fool of yourself. Especially police officers, they wouldn't dare to lightly criticize someone without knowing their background. One night, a person in plain clothes was walking on the road. A police officer stepped forward and inquired about their profession. The person said, "I am the Prime Minister." The police officer quickly stood at attention and saluted, assuming that someone calling themself the Prime Minister must be a Grand Scholar from the former Qing Dynasty or the Premier of the Republic of China. The person slowly said, "Hold on, don't salute yet. I haven't finished speaking. I am a boatman, one who has a 'Prime Minister's belly that can hold a boat.'"

During the New Life Movement era, the waiters in hotels didn't dare to judge social status by clothing. One day, a country bumpkin came to book a room. The waiter smiled ingratiatingly and asked the guest's profession. The person said, "I am a King." The waiter was greatly surprised, knowing that "King" was a nickname for a major capitalist. Whether it was the Steel King, the Petroleum King, or the Flour King, being called a King meant they had at least tens of millions in assets. So, he was very cautious and did his best to flatter the person. The person laughed and said, "Stop flattering me, I haven't finished speaking. I am an incense keeper in the King's Temple."

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 204

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Thirty-One: Three Battles in the White-Clad Charge Through the Snow Formation; The Entire Battalion Sacrifices, Red-Eyed, Into the Gunfire

Zi Qiang heard clearly that the sound of footsteps had passed four or five hundred meters. Then, estimating the enemy's distance, he ordered the machine gunners to begin firing. "Rat-tat-tat," the bullets hit the back of the enemy's column. They were walking in a column, not yet dispersed, and they suddenly encountered the enemy from behind. This was something they never dreamed of. Moreover, the village was already close ahead, and if they continued forward, they would certainly be attacked from that side as well. At this moment, a rushing sound suddenly arose in the enemy's formation, probably because they were running around in the snow. This unexpected attack would cause even heavenly soldiers and generals to panic, especially since some of the traitors were forced to come along, making them even more flustered. They turned around and followed up with a counterattack from the gully. When they counterattacked in this way, the defenders in the village knew that they had fallen into a trap and also fired at their line. The enemy commander knew that in this narrow terrain, they could not divide their forces to face the enemy on both sides. Therefore, he immediately ordered the invaders to disperse, lie down, and stop the counterattack. Zhao Ziqiang, on the gully above, directed his brothers to fire a volley, seeing that the enemy's bullets were returning erratically, high and low, clearly indicating scattered formations, and likely causing many casualties. After the enemy returned fire for a while, they retreated eastward and suddenly fell silent. If they were to continue shooting blindly, it would be a waste of bullets. In the troops outside the pass, losing a bullet was like losing a drop of blood, and it was not easy to get supplies. Therefore, Ziqiang also stopped shooting, using the bayonet of his rifle to raise a small white flag, waving it a few times towards the opposite bank. A platoon leader on the other side understood and also had a white object waving in the low air. So, Ziqiang led his brothers along the gully, slowly walking forward. The enemy, knowing that they had fallen into an ambush, did not expect the ambush to be only a company. Therefore, although they had retreated to the high ground east of the gully entrance, they were determined not to let the Chinese army get any closer to them. Ziqiang's company pressed forward, causing a slight disturbance. The enemy on that side, forced into this position, could not remain calm and also used machine guns to sweep the gully, while using the small cannons they had brought to bombard the distant village at the same time. Wimbledon's Fierce Battle

Men's Singles Reaches Final Four 205

Crawford and Four Others Qualify for Quarterfinals

Two American Youths Both Win and Advance

(Reuters, London, 2nd) Results of the Wimbledon tennis championships men's singles quarterfinals: Crawford, Shields, Vines, and Wood qualify for the quarterfinals. Results are as follows:

Crawford (Aus) (7-5, 2-6, 7-5, 6-0) Stephens (USA)

Crawford Defeats Stephens 206

Australian Crawford, the defending Wimbledon champion, defeated American Davis Cup player Stephens in a highly watched competition. Both sides had exceptionally powerful serves, and both struggled to counter each other. Stephens' control over his shots and speed especially amazed the audience. However, when Stephens led 5-4 in the third set, he suddenly collapsed, losing three consecutive games and the match. Crawford's victory was particularly commendable, as doctors had advised him not to participate. After the match, he had to be helped into the dressing room, completely exhausted. During the match, Crawford often showed signs of fatigue.

Shields Defeats Austin 207

American Davis Cup player Shields defeated British Austin in a dramatic five-set battle. Austin won the first two sets 6-4, 6-2, gaining a significant advantage with superior shots and speed. In the third set, Austin's ______ before this was ______ on ______ intensely ______. However, adding constant ______ caused Austin to make many mistakes. Shields then won two consecutive sets 7-5, 6-3, tying the match at two sets apiece. In the final decisive set, Austin took an early lead of 3-0, but Shields then tied the score. Austin then took the lead again at 5-4. At this point, Shields unleashed serves like cannonballs, tying the score again. Shields broke Austin's serve and ultimately won 7-5, ending the match in a sliding four. In the final game, Shields' shots deep into the corner and a cannonball serve were very impressive.

Vines Wins Over Lott in Four Sets 208

British Vines eliminated American Davis Cup player Lott, performing completely out of character, far from his usual brilliance. His victory over Lott was not due to his skill but entirely due to his stamina. Vines won the first set 6-4, lost the second set 2-6, and then won the final two sets 7-5, 10-8. In the fourth set, Lott led 5-2, but then suddenly became overwhelmed, succumbing to exhaustion and suffering a miserable defeat.

Wood Easily Defeats Kappel 209

American Wood easily defeated South African Kappel. He only lost the third set due to playing too fancy. In the final set, Wood was overwhelming, winning all six games. Kappel's defeat was marked by countless double faults. The overall score was 6-1, 6-4, 3-6, 6-0.

"Basic Gymnastics," a Sports Masterpiece Translated into Nine Languages, Published 222

The World's Newest Style of Danish Gymnastics

Compiled and Translated by the Physical Education Department of Ginling Women's University

Swedish gymnastics is on the path to decline, while Danish gymnastics is suitable for physiology and is the rising star. Currently, many countries in Europe and America are promoting its practice. In our country, it is still rare. The Physical Education Department of Ginling Women's Arts and Sciences University, recognizing this, specifically had the department's physical education professors, Ms. Yang Xiaorang and Ms. Wang Liming, translate a masterpiece by the famous Danish gymnast, Mr. Buk, into Chinese, titled "Basic Gymnastics."

The original work has been translated into as many as nine languages in European and American countries, its value and fame are self-evident. The book has rich contents and concise translations, for the value, goals, characteristics, educational methods, teaching material procedures, progressive methods of basic gymnastics, and its adaptive environmental elements, part names and descriptions, practice of flexibility, toughness, and training of cooperative ability and joint movements, is described earnestly and guided in detail, and attached with dozens of illustrations. The basic gymnastics is the newest and best academic, and has the effect of developing physical strength, correcting general bad postures and habits, so it is necessary for all schools above middle school to practice. The book is exquisitely printed in a volume using high-quality Daolin paper, priced at one dollar and two corners, with a special price of 10% off, and published by the Diligent Bookstore, 392 Father Lous Road, Shanghai.

Education News

Ministry of Education Inspector Zhong Daozan Reports on Key Points for Improving Vocational Education in Anhui Province 223

Three hours of instruction per week, with Chinese, mathematics, English, etc., for three years. Zhong's educational situation. This inspection report has been submitted to the Ministry of Education. The points regarding the urgent need for improvement in vocational education in the province are recorded below.

A. Regarding General Matters 224

1. Most school principals are not agricultural or industrial professionals, nor do they have excellent experience in vocational education, which clearly does not comply with regulations. A strict assessment should be conducted, and those who are unqualified and have no achievements in their work must be replaced and qualified personnel carefully selected to take over in order to improve the situation.

2. The practical training equipment in each school, such as farms, mulberry gardens, factories, silkworm rearing rooms, etc., is either too small to be used or the facilities are too simple to facilitate teaching. Their scope should be expanded and their content enriched to achieve practical results. If limited by funding and unable to increase the budget, the number of classes should be reduced according to the situation, or some or all of the student enrollment should be temporarily suspended and the remaining funds transferred to teaching equipment.

3. The practical training material fees for each school are mostly insufficient and the budget should be increased in accordance with regulations.

4. The teaching in each school mostly focuses on lectures, with very little time spent on practical training. Most schools also learn before practicing and the practical training time for each academic year gradually increases. Some practical training sessions only last two hours. All these methods are inconsistent with the regulations and should be improved as soon as possible.

5. Most students in each school are focused on higher education, but in reality, they often lack economic capacity. In order to adapt to the environment, schools often increase the types of general subjects and teaching hours, which is inconsistent with the purpose of vocational schools. Focus should be placed on skill-based subjects to cultivate sufficient production capacity in order to strengthen students' belief in their profession.

6. Students in each school produce a small number of products, and most of them are rough and of little commercial value. Even the better ones mostly imitate existing products on the market in terms of drawings, colors, and quality, lacking improvement and promotion of ideas.

7. Schools in each area mostly close themselves off and have little contact with vocational organizations. They also provide little training in students' automatic management and entrepreneurial cooperation spirit.

8. The teaching materials used in general subjects such as mathematics, Chinese, physics, and chemistry in each school cannot be linked to the vocational subjects being studied. The 20-minute break exercises each day should be held during practical work time to regulate students' physical and mental health, but the schools have not complied with this.

9. The clothing, food, housing, and transportation of the faculty and staff in each school mostly fail to demonstrate the spirit of hard work and perseverance to serve as an example for the students. They also rarely live with the students.

10. Students in schools in northern Anhui are quite frugal and hardworking, but have not yet developed habits of hygiene, cleanliness, tidiness, and labor.

11. Girls' vocational schools in the province provide meals and accommodation at the school to show preferential treatment, resulting in a large number of students. However, the concept of focusing on women's vocational training to cultivate the ability to be economically independent is still weak, often viewing it as a preparatory school for higher education.

The above points six to eleven should be improved.

B. Concerning Various Schools 225

1. Provincial First Vocational School, (1) Practical training time for all departments: first year is the least, second year is slightly more, third year accounts for about one-quarter of the total time. The Applied Chemistry Department in the first year has no practical training in making finished products other than chemical experiments. They should be required to first manufacture simple commodities such as chalk, soap paste, etc., to increase practical work. For the practical skills of the current students in each grade, holiday periods should be used as much as possible to intensify long-term practical work to make up for the deficiency. (2) In order for Civil Engineering students to obtain practical experience, they should, during the summer vacation of the third academic year, request construction agencies to send them to various local public works bureaus for on-site learning. The Applied Chemistry and Mechanical Engineering departments should conduct one or two similar long-term production operations to achieve proficiency in skills. (3) To strengthen the foundation and proficiency of vocational skills, high school graduates can be recruited for five or six years of training. The first two years should focus on general training, with vocational training equally emphasized. The fifth and sixth years should have vocational training for three hours per week. All three years have excessive hours for Chinese, Mathematics, and English, which should be corrected. (5) Library equipment is incomplete, especially reference books for various vocational subjects.

2. Provincial First Girls' Vocational School, (1) The practical training equipment for each department is very simple. The silkworm rearing and silk-making facilities are narrow, leaky, and dirty, making them unsuitable. The vacant land outside the facilities also lacks cleanliness. (2) Except for the Sericulture Department, the practical training time is less than one-quarter of the total time. Embroidery Department drawing is eight hours per week. All departments have English subjects arranged, which are inappropriate. (3) The achievements in embroidery and dyeing are mostly crude, except for a small portion that is still presentable. The patterns and colors are inferior to existing products on the market. Attention should be paid to research on fresh colors and styles. (4) Students throughout the school are more interested in general academic subjects than in vocational subjects, which urgently needs to be corrected.

3. Provincial Second Vocational School, (1) The commercial department's practical training equipment only has five English typewriters and a small school store. The learning time each week is also very limited. If the number of typewriters cannot be increased temporarily, after-school, evening, and weekend holidays should be used to intensify learning in rotating groups and should be concentrated for learning, not extended to two years, which would lead to inefficient learning. (5) Considering the environment of Wuhu, there is no need to run advanced commerce. It should be changed to junior commerce and commercial tutoring, and should also include old-style bookkeeping, attention to calligraphy in advertisement, abacus calculation, and commodity research, etc., to seek practicality. (3) Agricultural equipment is very simple, and there is no new-style agricultural tool or agronomy practice. There is only rice cultivation and horticulture, only ordinary vegetables, with nothing to improve or promote. The original farmland area is not extensive, and the practice is only eleven hours per week. Students' work habits have not yet been developed.

4. Provincial Seventh Vocational School, (1) The school building of the second division was converted from the Water Conservancy Bureau. The rooms are small and very unsuitable. The dyeing and leather-making factories are very simple in equipment. Often two or three people share one machine, taking turns to learn, and the time is very uneconomical. (2) The leather-making achievements are very crude, almost unsalable. The products that are better and can be sold often have excessive losses. The dyeing and weaving products are also very scarce. (3) Because the school's material costs are insufficient, each sheet of cowhide is often divided into three or four sheets for group learning. The cowhide that has been divided is often unable to be sold. (4) The school has a total of six classes in two departments. This year's enrollment should be suspended once, and all funds from the two classes, about ten thousand yuan, should be allocated for equipment, or concentrate financial resources to run the Applied Chemistry Department specifically, dividing it into two groups: leather making and leather goods. The dyeing and weaving equipment should be converted into a vocational supplementary department. (1) For students in existing classes who lack sufficient practice, the method of the aforementioned Provincial First Vocational School can be referred to for handling.

5. Provincial Fourth Vocational School, (1) The mulberry garden is forty mu, and the farmland owned and rented is only thirty-four mu in total. Recently, the Department of Education allocated funds to purchase farmland, which is currently being negotiated. In the past, there were no achievements to speak of. (2) There is no new-style agricultural equipment, and the facilities are simple, so they urgently need to be purchased. (3) Nurseries, wheat fields, vegetable gardens, etc., still need to be intensified for management, and the amount of production is also small. (4) Student dormitories are very unclean, and clothes and bedding are also too dirty.

6. Private Anhui Vocational School, (1) The school's mechanical and dyeing departments both have quite suitable equipment. Compared with the existing number of students and practical training equipment, each can still add more than twenty people. Vocational supplementary classes or dozens of apprentices should be recruited to specialize in production and business, and to provide vocational supplementary education. (2) After the opening of the Wuhu Zha Road, more people apply to the school for mechanical engineering than for dyeing, and some request to pay their own expenses. (3) The school’s lectures and practical training each account for half, and the allocation is still appropriate. However, among the courses taught, English, mathematics, Chinese, etc., account for too much, and vocational subjects are too few. (4) The school has a good foundation, but it lacks funds abnormally. In addition to the Department of Education’s annual subsidy of 13,000 yuan, there is almost no other income. It should be brought under the Department's management or raise more funds for expansion. (5) The women's simplified department graduates in one year, studying sewing, embroidery, and weaving. The time is short and the subjects are numerous. Although practical results are achieved, the time limit should be extended, and it should be divided into two groups, sewing and embroidery, and weaving, and renamed the Women's Junior Vocational Department or recruit older illiterate women to run a home arts vocational supplementary class.

Chinese Marine Biological Society 226

Actively Researching Production and Education

Marine organisms have great value both academically and economically. However, the Chinese people have historically not conducted research on marine organisms and passively watched as strong neighbors fish and collect their benefits in Chinese waters. Those with aspirations for research, aware of this, established the Chinese Marine Biological Society in Xiamen five years ago, dedicated to researching marine organisms and promoting knowledge of marine biology. Since its establishment, with the assistance of the China Cultural Fund Society and the American Rockefeller Foundation, and in cooperation with Xiamen University, many domestic biology experts have been invited to Xiamen during past summer holidays to conduct surveys and research on local marine organisms. As for this year's association affairs, they have been expanded slightly compared to the past, and are being conducted in three areas:

(1) Summer research on marine specialties of the coastal Qingdao and Xiamen areas of our country. This year, in addition to continuing cooperation with Xiamen University, it has also been invited to join in cooperation by the newly established Qingdao Marine Biology Research Institute. Therefore, this year's summer research will be conducted simultaneously in Qingdao and Xiamen. The summer research session will be from July 8th to August 18th. The biology experts invited to participate in the research in Qingdao include Professor Dai Lisheng of Tsinghua University (Protozoa), Professor Zhang Feng of the National Peiping Research Institute (Mollusks), and Professor Lu Dingheng (Pseudomollusks), Professor Zhang Chunlin of the Peiping Jing Sheng Biological Survey Institute (Fish), and Professor Li Liangqing (Algae), Professor Zhang Kui of Qilu University (Coelenterates), and Professor Xu Yinqi of Soochow University (Parasitology). Those going to Xiamen have invited Professor Tang Peisong of Wuhan University (Physiology), Professor Zheng Zuoxin of Fuzhou Union University (Embryology), Professor Zhu Xi of Guangzhou Sun Yat-sen University (Embryology), Professor Chen Tongbai of the Agricultural and Forestry Bureau of the Guangdong Construction Department (Fish), Professor Chen Xintao of Lingnan University (Parasitology), Professor Wu Zhaofa of Henan University (Animal Morphology), Professor Huang Wenfeng of Xiamen Jimei College (Fisheries), and Professor Chen Ziying of the Biology Department of Xiamen University, Lin Shaowen, and others.

(2) Summer Marine Biology Remedial Class is jointly organized by the Association and the Biology Department of Xiamen University, specifically for science teachers in secondary schools. This class focuses on field observation. If this year's results are satisfactory, it will continue to be established in the future.

(3) Annual Research is planned to be conducted at the coastal biological museum of Xiamen University. The candidates have not yet been determined. However, the research problems must have considerable economic value. Although the Association is a purely academic organization, it also thinks about contributing to domestic production.

Shandong Students' Military Training Begins, More Than 2,000 Students Are Armed 227

Han Fuqu Holds Meeting for Training

(Jinan Correspondence) More than 2,000 high school students in the province are concentrated in Jinan, Yidu, and Yanzhou for military training. Students from various places arrived at the designated locations by armored train or long-distance bus. More than 230 students from Qingdao Shandong University also arrived in Yidu by armored train today (1st) to join the army. Training will begin tomorrow (2nd). Those concentrated in Jinan are organized into two battalions. The first battalion is at Qilu Middle School in Dongguan, and the second battalion is at Qilu University in Nanguan. The students live in the dormitories of the two schools. The students of Qilu University who had an earlier vacation have gone home, and will return to school successively today and tomorrow. The students have been divided into battalions, companies, and platoons yesterday and have assembled once to be taught basic movements, commands, and etiquette by the training officers. After entering the dormitory, roll call is taken, and they are not allowed to go out. Each officer uses military law to restrain them, which is very strict. The main office buildings are temporarily used as battalion headquarters. Each room in the dormitory houses three people, completely using the floor as a bed, with one mattress and one sheet per person. Some bring pillows, but the battalion commander does not allow it, ordering them to take off their shoes and socks every night and wrap them in a bundle to use as pillows. There are only toiletries in the room, nothing else. It is extremely simple and completely militarized. This morning (1st), the Military Training Committee issued military uniforms and symbols, and everyone was fully armed for a time. From 1:30 pm to 3:00 pm, they assembled for training. After dinner, from 5:00 pm to 7:00 pm, they still assembled for training. All basic movements have already been practiced by the students at school, so retraining is easier. Only those with improper posture are corrected. Because the provincial governor Han Fuqu is scheduled to assemble all the students undergoing training at the Provincial Sports Field at 7:00 am tomorrow (2nd) for a speech, a rehearsal of saluting postures and marching movements was conducted today, and there will be a grand occasion at that time. Guns will also be issued for practice.

China Cooperative Society Notice to Members to Convene Annual Meeting 232

All Proposals and Papers to be Sent to the Society Before September

The China Cooperative Society issued a notice stating that the Society, through the resolution of the Third Executive Committee, will convene the Fourth Members' Congress, and through the resolution of the First Meeting of the Society, it has been decided to hold it at the new Society headquarters in the capital for four consecutive days starting on October 7th. It is hoped that all comrades will take time out of their busy schedules to attend and jointly promote the cooperative cause in our country. It is greatly anticipated. All proposals or papers to be presented at the meeting should be sent to the Society before September 10th for organization. However, the intention of the proposals must be appropriate to actual needs, the reasons must be concise, and the methods must be thorough and easy to implement. As for the papers, they should provide materials for discussion in the various group discussion meetings at the meeting, and the scope is limited to four areas: cooperative laws and regulations, cooperative insurance, cooperative practices, and cooperative education. The content should be based on national conditions and facilitate implementation. If there are actual experiences that merely list various difficult problems for submission to the various group discussion meetings, they are also welcome. However, the difficult circumstances of each problem must be explained systematically, and the nature of the problem must be able to be incorporated into any one of the above four discussion areas and be relatively important. All of these aspects are the key points to which this Congress pays special attention. It is hoped that you will be informed. Regarding special prices for train and ship travel for members attending the meeting, we have respectively consulted with the Ministry of Railways and Communications to provide preferential treatment. In addition to separate letters of notification, we will issue another notice and hope that you will fill in each item listed on the reply slip immediately after receiving this Society's notice and send it to the Society to facilitate preparation. We look forward to it. The Preparatory Committee of the Fourth Annual Meeting of the China Cooperative Society.

The Sixth Jiangsu People's Education District is Eager to Develop Livelihood Education 234

Taking the Promotion of Cooperative Undertakings as the Central Work

The Work Plan Has Been Approved by the Social Education Council

The Sixth Jiangsu Province People's Education District discussed livelihood education at this Social Education Research Conference and approved a plan to take the promotion of cooperative undertakings as the central work of livelihood education. The original plan is recorded as follows:

Introduction 235

The implementation of people's education should start with livelihood education. Observing our country's society, this has been generally recognized by us and there is an urgent need in fact. All educational facilities that benefit livelihood, such as the improvement of production technology, the promotion of excellent varieties, the advocacy of rural sideline occupations, the regulation of civilian finance, and everything else, people's education agencies are doing their best to make the undertaking universal and to seek rapid efficiency. Although there are many undertakings and it is difficult to do everything at once, funds and talents are often insufficient. For the present, the key is to have a single goal, organize the people as the object of education, observe their common economic needs, and engage in the improvement of production. Then, taking the promotion of cooperative undertakings as an important method of implementing livelihood education, everyone will be benefited.

Basic 236

(A) Taking the basic education area as the starting area for cooperative undertakings, promoting industrial cooperation methods (1) Regarding the agricultural or industrial situation of the basic education area, select a widespread and beneficial undertaking, investigate its production and sales situation, and design and promote improvement, that is, take guiding the organization of cooperative societies as the experimental center and train its members. (2) The affairs of the cooperative society shall be handled by full-time personnel sent by the guiding agency to assist in the handling, so as to reduce the burden of the cooperative society and gradually enable it to operate independently, and a considerable percentage may be stipulated under the people's education undertaking fund for the promotion of cooperative undertakings. (3) In addition to the elected officials, the cooperative society should recruit trainees to undertake the actual training of cooperation, so as to cultivate the backbone of promoting cooperative undertakings in the area. The food allowances for trainees are borne by the guiding agency. (4) Before the business of the cooperative society is developed, it can be divided into several periods in a year, and operated in stages according to the needs of the members. (5) The business of the cooperative society should be mainly based on the common needs of the members. Credit, purchase, transportation, sales, utilization, and other businesses are all methods and conditions for completing industrial cooperation, and help the implementation of production cooperation, but there must be a fixed business center, so that each business has a chain relationship, in order to avoid danger. (6) Set a suitable period to hold training courses for members to receive livelihood education. (7) Based on the cooperative situation of the members, conduct precise economic surveys and statistics to guide the members in preparing an annual income and expenditure budget, in order to seek the improvement and improvement of the members' lives in terms of knowledge. The guiding agency should jointly handle various educational undertakings for training members with the business committee of the cooperative society.

Promotion 237

(B) The cooperative undertakings in the promotion area should be factually linked to the cooperative center organization in the basic education area, and the methods are as follows: (1) Assign qualified personnel trained in the basic education area to the promotion area to take responsibility for promotion. (2) The cooperative societies in the promotion area independently organize their nature and purpose, which must be the same as the cooperative societies in the basic education area in whole or in part. (3) The cooperative society in the promotion area obtains the corporate members of the cooperative society in the basic education area, or the cooperative societies in the promotion area jointly organize a cooperative society union with the cooperative societies in the basic education area. (4) The guiding agency, which unifies the promotion of cooperative undertakings in the education area in the form of a union, applies most of its strength to the union to seek the universality of educational efficiency.

Page 19

Free Talk

The Road of the Mass Language Movement 240

— Tao Xingzhi

Mr. Hu Yuzhi's explanation of mass language is very good. I would like to suggest a correction of two words. Mass language is the language that represents the progressive consciousness of the masses. Mass writing is the writing that represents the progressive consciousness.

Mass language and mass writing must be united... united in degree, united in need, and united in consciousness.

When mass language and writing suit the level, needs, and consciousness of the masses, the reaction of the masses themselves is joy. Therefore, mass language and writing are the language and writing that the masses are happy to say, happy to hear, happy to write, and happy to read. This state of joy is the realm of art.

A month ago, I borrowed a reel of film from a film company and sent it to the countryside for public screening. We wanted to teach the farmers to read the instructions a few days before the screening. Although the instructions were written in vernacular Chinese, the local schoolteachers could not teach it, and the farmers could not read it. I had no choice but to rewrite a set of instructions to teach everyone. This was not easy. I had to revise the manuscript several times before I could barely complete it. According to the local schoolteacher, the instructions I finally wrote were still too difficult. But it was at least ten times easier than the original manuscript from the film company. This example shows that the vernacular Chinese that is currently circulating is simply replacing the "zhi hu zhe ye" of classical Chinese with "de ma a ya," adding some foreign grammar and the consciousness of some young masters and young ladies, new scholars, and doctors. In writing, this kind of vernacular Chinese is incomprehensible to the masses; in reading, it is unintelligible to the masses. We can see that there is a great dark curtain in the Chinese literary movement: vernacular Chinese is not united with mass language.

The masses live a life of symbolic poverty. But their need for symbols is an undeniable fact. Old women use knots to keep accounts. Farmers carve tree bark to express their emotions. Wild children write "wang ba dan" to scold people. Students in people's schools use phonetic symbols to replace characters they cannot write. This need can be further illustrated by a story. Once, a woman sent a letter to her husband. When the husband opened it, he saw that the paper was drawn with...

"A single circle, a double circle, a circle, a broken circle, a series of circles."

The husband could not understand it. A clever man pointed out the secret of the circles drawn by his wife and said...

"I wanted to send my love, but I had no way to send it, so I drew a few circles instead. The single circle is me. The double circle is you. The round circle is reunion. The broken circle is separation. And there are endless thoughts that I express by circling all the way to the end."

These examples indicate that there is a great deficiency in the lives of the masses. The masses do not have enough symbols for thought, symbols for emotion, and symbols for action... in short, they do not have enough symbols for life. The symbols of the masses are as meager as their bread. Those who exploit the masses' bread are also monopolizing the symbols needed for the masses' lives.

In this light, the mass language movement has two main paths to follow...

(1) Intellectuals participate in the life of the masses, and on the basis of the evolution of mass language, strive to write mass writing that unites language and writing;

(2) Popularize the symbols of life among the masses so that the masses themselves can create mass writing that unites language and writing.

Intellectuals who want to write mass writing must first learn mass language. They must worship the masses as teachers. Not enough! They must delve into the life of the masses, share their lives, and share their joys and sorrows. They must be soldiers in the ranks of the masses. Only when their own lives are integrated with the lives of the masses can they appreciate the joys and sorrows of the lives of the masses; only then can writing about the masses be writing about themselves, and writing about themselves be writing about the masses. If they disdain to worship the masses as teachers and refuse to be a private in the ranks of the masses, they will never write good mass writing.

What symbols should be popularized among the masses? Chinese characters? Phonetic symbols? Pinyin writing? My suggestion is to do all three: Chinese characters should be taught; phonetic symbols should be taught; and mass writing spelled out with phonetic symbols should be taught even more.

Chinese characters are the treasure of the scholar-officials. The masses must recognize this treasure in order to see through the mystery of the scholar-officials. There are eighty million people who can teach Chinese characters. Although Chinese characters themselves are difficult to learn, the large number of people who can teach these symbols is a great convenience for the promotion movement. I believe that it is enough to simply recognize Chinese characters. One way to help the masses recognize Chinese characters is with phonetic symbols. If the masses learn phonetic symbols, they can automatically use dictionaries, recognize new words, and pursue new knowledge. But we cannot stop there. We must immediately teach the masses to use phonetic symbols to record their own thoughts, feelings, and actions. We must immediately teach the masses to use phonetic symbols to write mass writing. Our purpose in teaching Chinese characters is to enable the masses to understand the China that is surrounded by Chinese characters; our purpose in teaching phonetic symbols, in a small sense, is to help them learn more Chinese characters, and in a large sense, is to use the method of cicada molting to create pinyin characters to replace Chinese characters, in order to produce pinyin mass writing.

When we are doing the work of popularizing written symbols, we should also promote vulgar written simplified Chinese characters, unify printed and handwritten fonts, and unify standard and cursive scripts, in order to save learning time and energy.

Students in primary and secondary schools and people's schools should all become little teachers, each teaching at least two illiterate people. In this way, we will have more than ten million organized people to take on the important task of popularizing symbols. In addition, with the further cultivation and general mobilization of the eighty million literate masses, within a few years, the masses will be able to obtain the symbols they need for life.

When the masses obtain symbols, they will be able to describe their lives in detail. There will be literary geniuses in the ranks of the masses. They will naturally produce first-class mass writing.

When we transmit written symbols to the masses, we must do a "filtering" job. We must filter out outdated ideas, filter out numbing toxins, filter out the classics, and filter out foreign grammar. The symbols we offer to the masses should be like clean water without microorganisms. When the masses obtain these clean water symbols, they will be able to freely, without prejudice, write true mass writing.

I would like to point out that mass language must be based on a living language. The living language that three-quarters of the Chinese can understand is filtered Mandarin Chinese. Mandarin Chinese is also the most pleasant to listen to, and people are willing to learn it. Therefore, Mandarin Chinese is indeed qualified to become the main component of mass language. But mass language should be bold. Any local dialects, and even foreign languages, that have a close relationship with the progressive life of the masses can be absorbed as much as possible. We do not need to suspend an abstract and subjective standard and forcibly take or discard them. Let the masses choose for themselves. Those that do not suit the taste of the progressive masses will be naturally eliminated, and we do not need to worry too much.

The masses with progressive consciousness should lead the masses with backward consciousness to improve their lives... improve their level, improve their needs, and improve their consciousness. In this way, mass language can continue to improve, and mass writing will follow it and continue to improve.
