— TK

Good News for Readers! 242

— Gao Lu

I remember the day I saw the brochure of the China Dental Protection Association at a friend's house, which also had several red characters printed on it noting the cost. At that time, my friend was suffering from a toothache, so we discussed it and decided to join the association at the same time. The membership fee was paid to the Shanghai Bank designated by the association to collect it. I myself did not spend any money (because the association's articles stipulate that the introducer can join as an equal member for free) and became a member, which brought me many benefits. I think the association is willing to provide universal service, and since it has been sent to all walks of life, many people must have seen this brochure. However, this preferential method will end on July 10th. I hope you will join the association as soon as possible, so that you can also share the benefits. The address of the association is on the third floor of No. 47 Ningbo Road, at the intersection of Jiangxi Road, Shanghai. The editor notes that the association's organization is purely service-oriented, so all the benefits for members are very preferential. Mr. Gao Feng introduced eight friends to the association, and also joined for free at the same time, and has a considerable understanding and goodwill towards the association, which is by no means comparable to empty publicity. I think that in the current high tide of the New Life Movement, the importance of dental care is already stipulated in the implementation of the convention. However, the people's economy is already so depressed, and to get the proper method of dental protection, it is necessary to join the association. However, the effective period of this preferential method is very short. If you intend to join, I hope you will do so as soon as possible, and do not miss this good opportunity!

Regarding Jin Shengtan's Annotated Water Margin (Part 1) 243

— Yu Yangling

In the "Trends" on June 30th, there is an article by Mr. Er Ye, "On the Emergence and Growth of Vernacular Chinese." I agree with the main idea of ​​the full text, but I have a slightly different opinion from Mr. Er Ye on the section about Jin Shengtan's annotation of Water Margin. This issue is worth discussing, so I will also talk about it.

First, let's look at Mr. Er Ye's original text...

For example, "Water Margin" is a famous novel, the result of many years of struggle in suffering, and its most valuable point is that it is written in spoken language. However, what did our Master Jin Shengtan say? He said that this is a "talented scholar's book," and he insisted on putting it together with Zuo Shi and Zhuang Sao! And there is something in the book that does not resemble the consciousness of the noble group - the robbers are not born bad people, but the official masters are bad people, forcing people to become robbers - he simply could not bear it. So he tampered with it, he wanted to "seal Hangu Pass with mud pills," he insisted on creating some "profound meanings and great righteousness" and "Spring and Autumn Annals writing style" in the book. In my opinion, Jin Shengtan put Water Margin and Zuo Shi and Zhuang Sao together and respected it as a "talented scholar's book," there was no malice in it, but a very correct view, just like the current critics value the novels that describe rickshaw pullers. As for "talented scholar's book," it is just a common term used by the Ming people, just like today's people often say "genius" and "great man." If Jin Shengtan used the "consciousness of the noble group" to select books, he would never have selected Water Margin. Moreover, he selected Water Margin and cut the complete one hundred and twenty chapter version, which was purely a series of stories, into seventy chapters. This is a purposeful work, the purpose of which is to expose the darkness of bureaucratic politics, point out the social causes of the Liangshanbo group, and praise the righteousness of the vagrant class. He ridiculed Song Jiang, who was written as very loyal and righteous in the story and only hoped to be recruited, to nothing. May I ask what kind of consciousness is this? In the fifty-first chapter of Water Margin, when writing about the uncle-brother-in-law of Gao Qiu's uncle bullying people, Jin Shengtan wrote...

Gao Qiu can do anything, but it can still be limited... Gao Qiu's uncle-brothers can do anything, how can it be limited? Gao Qiu's uncle-brothers can do anything, but it can still be limited; Gao Qiu's uncle-brothers also have relatives, and they can do anything again, how can it be limited? Gao Qiu's uncle-brothers also have relatives and can do anything again, but it can still be limited; Gao Qiu's uncle-brothers' relatives must also have their jackals and dogs running around, and they must all be able to do anything, how can it be limited? Alas! The world is the world of the court, and the people are the children of the court; now, if we allow unlimited tigers and wolves to open their unlimited greedy mouths, to seize unlimited muscles, to fill unlimited valleys, and want the people not to rebel and the country not to perish, how can we get it! "

This paragraph illustrates the unlimited exploitation under bureaucratic politics and its inevitable consequences, how can it be said to be out of the "consciousness of the noble group?"

From Guangzhou to Shanghai (Part 3) 244

— Pu Feng

"Stop! Walk to the right!" As I walked past that distinguished compatriot, I not only heard this voice, but also received a push from his distinguished hand.

"What? What do you do?" I opened my eyes wide; watching my friend, wearing an inverted collar, passed the customs first, unwilling, and walked to the left again.

Thank God, learning two sentences of foreign language did work after all, and this time I was not blocked. This made me understand the great truth of why everyone has to desperately learn two sentences of foreign language.

X X X X X

Get off the ship.

At the pier, I was stopped by the inspectors, but I was not inspected. I thought it was due to the inverted collar on my body, and I was quite proud. When I got on the ship, it did not start at the departure time shown on the sign. I felt strangely anxious sitting there waiting.

"Woo woo!" The whistle sounded, but the ship did not move. I only saw a red-haired devil leading a group of majestic, ragged comrades, holding inspection equipment in their hands.

"Open the box! Quickly!" An extremely urgent order.

"Student, there is nothing in it," I replied.

"Quickly! Open, ......"

I had to open it. I saw him touching with both hands and looking down with his eyes. There was nothing to blackmail, so he became polite... "Sorry! Doing things for the public, I have to look!"

The inspector went aside.

"Open it quickly! ... Use a knife."

A student's leather suitcase tied with a rope was actually cut open, and the things were taken out one by one.

He left. The student showed a mourning face, stepping on the box with his feet because it could not be covered due to his turning it over, and his eyes were spitting fire.

X X X X X

"For my own viewing, not a commodity, ......" A group of people surrounded a student, he said this in incorrect Mandarin.

"Erotic pictures! Prohibited items, ... Go ashore!" A threatening situation.

"For my own viewing, ......"

"Five dollars, quickly!"

"Less please!" A pleading voice.

In the end, the inspector walked away again, with three Hong Kong dollars newly put in his pocket.

The ship has not yet started, but the inspector has gone to another place. The student who was blackmailed was saying words to comfort himself, such as I originally planned to go ashore to see the old foreigners, such as I really wanted to tear it up immediately, such as ......, turning his head, I saw that he secretly tore up the remaining two erotic pictures in his hand.

Notice to Mr. Pu Feng... "From Guangzhou to Shanghai" manuscript, since it is known by letter that it has been published in another publication, it will be stopped tomorrow. As for whether the manuscript received by this publication is the one that Mr. Pu Feng "entrusted someone to find a place to publish and lost," please go to the editorial department of this publication to check the original manuscript.

Correction In yesterday's article by Mr. Wang Renshu, line 90, "as Mr. Hu Shih said," it was found that "Shih" was misprinted as "Yu," which was not corrected in time. We hereby correct it.

Flour Futures: Bulls Gradually Unload 255

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, the market for all months showed signs of weakening, as quoted prices for foreign wheat in Chicago fell significantly by about 7 or 8 jiao. Although the weather in the local area remains scorching hot, heavy rain in the north has brought hope to Beijing and Tianjin. Moreover, non-industry factors seem to be losing momentum, and the inflated prices driven by speculative bulls must eventually be supported by real sales. The difficulty in boosting flour sales after a bumper harvest in the north was already expected. The lifelessness of Tianjin indicates that the inflated flour prices have already been set up for an inevitable fall. Therefore, after the market opened yesterday, bulls gradually began to give up. Major factories, such as Fuxin and Fufeng, also had to gradually hedge their sales due to slow sales. Rumors that the factories would be collecting warehouse rental fees further unnerved the bulls, causing the decline in near-term contracts to be more severe than that of distant contracts. The quoted price for spot flour in Tianjin yesterday was 2.215 yuan (previously 2.245 yuan), which is similar to the standard price in this city. As a result, this month's contracts fell by another 2.75 li, August's contracts fell by 2.25 li, September's contracts fell by 2 li, and October to December's contracts fell by 1.75 li.

Abundant Wheat Arrivals Cause Standard Prices to Soften 256

Yesterday, the wheat futures market showed a weak and spiritless trend in all months after opening in the morning and afternoon. Market prices in the producing areas have gradually softened, and arrivals of goods have been abundant. In this city, ships and vehicles are abnormally congested, gradually causing concerns about stockpiles. Abundant wheat arrivals must be balanced by brisk flour sales in order to regulate the market. However, currently, wheat is abundant while flour sales are sluggish, inevitably causing obstacles. Therefore, those with physical goods have been hedging their sales on the exchange. If factory demand remains weak, this situation will become increasingly difficult. As a result, prices for each month gradually declined after the market opened. However, there has been no rain in this city, and bulls still have some strength to resist, so the decline was not as dramatic as the previous day. As a result, the price of this month's contracts fell by 3 fen, September's contracts fell by 5 fen, and October and November's contracts fell by 4 fen. Due to stockpiles and sluggish sales, the price of spot wheat has fallen by 3 to 5 fen in the central market. Wheat from Bengbu is priced at 3 yuan, wheat from Daqiao is priced at 2.9 jiao, and lower-quality wheat is priced at 2.8 jiao. Abundant Local Wheat Harvest 257

丨Unseen in the Last Decade丨

This year's wheat harvest is the best in the last decade, especially in Shaanxi, where the abundance of goods along the Longhai Railway has no outlet. Therefore, industry insiders predict that this city will become a central hub. The recent types of wheat arriving here seem to confirm this, such as the eastward flow of wheat from Xinyang County and Hankou, the continuous southward flow from Xuzhou and Linhuai Guan, and the unprecedented abundance of wheat produced in southern and northern Anhui. Therefore, this year's wheat production will be more than enough to supply the needs of the factories in this city. Furthermore, non-industry individuals initially believed that the rise in American wheat meant that foreign wheat could not be imported to China, and that, based on past experiences, there was no way to address the situation without foreign wheat. On the surface, this seemed reasonable, but in reality, it was likely not the case. The vastness of China's agricultural land and the amount of production often exceed people's expectations. For example, soybeans were once relied on from the three northeastern provinces, but since the establishment of Manchukuo, that source has been cut off. Initially, those involved were concerned that a shortage would inevitably cause panic. But China was blessed, and there was a full harvest in Jinpu and Longhai, and the supply was more than enough, and the price also fell along with various other prices. This is a well-known fact, and it is generally acknowledged by those who understand the environment. Therefore, even if this year's wheat production is compared to the quantity of borrowed wheat in the past, it is likely to be higher. With this proportion, it is very clear that the price of wheat cannot be arbitrarily raised.

Lower Reach Rice Sales Stagnant, Prices Weak 258

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the source estimated that more than 30 firms had arrived (approximately 5,000 shi of goods). Sentiment seemed to be watchful. Local shop demand suddenly turned stagnant, and demand from customers also tended to stop. The market currently shows a softening trend, mainly because sellers with more goods were willing to lower prices to sell quickly. However, some were unwilling to sell lightly due to the extremely dry weather, so the market situation became chaotic. Prices of thick and thin japonica rice fell by varying amounts, such as 1 jiao, 1.2 or 3 jiao. Du Yangjian and Yin Bian Yuan also moved according to the thoughts of individuals, so the general trend was the same as the japonica rice market, but the price drop was not as severe, only fluctuating by a few jiao.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, more than ten firms arrived from various locations in the lower reaches. Due to the hot weather, few shops were open in the market, leading to weak demand. The market showed that early thin japonica rice prices were short by 1 or 2 jiao, white yuan was weak by a few fen, and yangjian dujian was slightly weaker, while prices for the port customer tip were level.

Inland Inquiries and Customer Coarse Rice 259

Yesterday, the market for guest indica rice was sluggish, and the stock of guest indica foreign rice was sufficient. Guest indica rice continued to arrive in small quantities, and foreign rice was also returned from other ports. The tense situation in the market due to the drought has changed. Yesterday, due to the sluggishness of guest goods, prices fell. However, inland firms such as Wuxi and Zhejiang had inquiries about customer sales of machine-milled rice. There was also business on this street, with a total of 2,500 bags of Shashi coarse rice and Hunan machine-milled rice being transacted. This street also sold 500 bags of Xiaowen rice. The Fuzhou firm has been sluggish for a long time, and yesterday only 88 bags of coarse red rice were sold, and there were no other transactions. Therefore, although the market is currently weak, if customer sales are clear again today and tomorrow, it is feared that prices will have to be reduced again.

Tung Oil Market: Foreign Firms Actively Buying White Tung Oil 260

丨Domestic Sales Still Show No Signs of Momentum丨

Recently, white tung oil prices are reflecting activity from foreign firms during their half-year closing. There has been little activity in Hankou, with the end-of-month traded price at 29.3 yuan. After adding 29.6 yuan in foreign regulations, there were 200-300 tons of transactions. Traders opened at 23.78 yuan for Xiang tung and 23.56 yuan for Southern branch, both customer regulations, with approximately 1,000 dan traded. After a three-day market closure, there may still be large-volume transactions, as foreign firms are expected to continue actively buying. However, due to the continuous dry weather, domestic sales have been greatly affected. Jiangxi and Zhejiang provinces have not had rain for a long time, and seedlings are wilting. Farmers are busy drawing water to irrigate seedlings, and have no time to take care of lacquerware. The stagnation of domestic tung oil sales is therefore the reason. Although stockpiles in this city are low, there is little interest in importing due to the lack of sales. If there is ample rainfall, sales will definitely pick up. Therefore, when sellers are encountered, they are negotiated to replenish stockpiles. In the past one to two days, a customer from Hangzhou came to Shanghai to sell goods with sufficient oil content, with 26.6 yuan per stone offered for delivery in Shanghai, with a total of 1,500 to 1,600 stones being transacted. Reportedly, 500 stones were purchased by a certain grain firm to offset debts to a foreign firm, while the rest were purchased by tung oil firms. It is said that goods from Zhejiang are no longer popular, and there is also a foreign firm outlet in this city, although it is a small amount, it is enough to add color to the market. Therefore, even if domestic sales are slightly clear in the future, it is feared that it will be difficult to expect prices to be too low.

Sugar Market: Domestically Produced Green and Red Sugar Rise in Unison 261

Yesterday, after the announcement of the revised tariff, there were no increases or decreases, so sentiment turned stable, and trading in all sugars was very active. The guild set the market for No. 24 coarse white sugar at 20 yuan, and stock at this warehouse at 20.1 yuan, up 1 jiao, and local factory white sugar at 18.8 yuan, also up 1.15 jiao, all with transactions. Taikoo sugar B mark was offered at 20.06 yuan, and spot goods were scarce. Guangdong firms opened with more than 500 bags of Hainan red sugar, with the price still at 12.8 yuan, and the market trend was firm. Chaozhou firms opened with 400-500 bags of green sugar, with prices such as Longjiang green at 12.2 yuan and Shang Huanggang at 12.89 yuan, all up 2 or 3 jiao from before. Firms, considering the thin bottom, and the high price in Shantou, believe that they will not trade if they do not add 3 or 4 jiao. The market is tight, and Zhiyang also opened with more than 100 bags, with prices ranging from 15.5 yuan to 15.7 yuan. The market is also expected to continue to rise.

Silk and Tea: Refined and High-Quality Green Teas Selling Well in Europe 262

Yesterday, the local foreign firm tea market saw activity from British firms such as Tian Yu, Jinlong, and Xie He, as well as the China Tea Company, in buying refined and high-quality green teas from Tunxi, Wuyuan, and Shexian. The market for these teas was not sluggish. However, the opening price offered by sellers for high-quality goods from the eastern part of Wuyuan was only 180 yuan, while Tunxi goods were reduced to 160-170 yuan, and Shexian goods were reduced to 150-160 yuan, all down 12 or 13 yuan from last week. The market for ordinary green teas still showed no improvement. Transactions for pearl tea and gongxi were also scarce. Although traders have recently sent telegrams for Qifu black tea, the situation is stagnant, and tea prices continue to fall without rising.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

The Understanding That Should Be Had in Constructing "Mass Vernacular Literature" 264

— Ruo Sheng

The "Mass Vernacular" issue, arising from the "Classical Chinese" vs. "Vernacular Chinese" debate, has been vigorously discussed in recent days. The raising of this issue at the current stage undoubtedly has very practical significance and urgent need.

Language and writing are originally just products of the human social process. If the foundation of society undergoes changes, then the language and writing that represent social consciousness must gradually change accordingly. Otherwise, it will become an obstacle to social evolution. Now, in our society, the old is rapidly declining, and the new is gradually growing. To express this new consciousness, there should naturally be a new language and writing emerging, and this is the "Mass Vernacular."

However, judging from the various aspects of the discussion these past few days, opinions on this issue are still very inconsistent. We believe that "Mass Vernacular Literature" is not only absolutely against "Classical Chinese" 丨丨 representing "feudal consciousness", but also relatively against "Vernacular" 丨丨 the currently popular vernacular representing "bureaucratic comprador consciousness" or the like. To carry out these dual tasks, we must first seek a thorough understanding of the social relations of language development and the language itself, recognizing the opposition and unity between them. Therefore, many people now think that "Classical Chinese Revival" is of little significance, or that "Mass Vernacular Literature" is only against "Classical Chinese" and not against "Vernacular," only seeing one side of things without seeing the whole picture.

The so-called "Classical Chinese Revival" now, although only a dying struggle of a declining class, will not have much future. But if you do not thoroughly eliminate it, it will hinder the progress of the entire language. It's like a room with a person suffering from a very dangerous infectious disease, or a corpse that has already died. If you don't quickly send it to the hospital or bury it, how harmful it is to the rest of the healthy people. Similarly, the ghosts and monsters of this old Chinese language are now reappearing in disguise, making trouble and bewitching people everywhere. Even healthy people like Mr. Le Sibing will be bewitched by them, not to mention how many others! (See Freedom Forum, June 23rd) Therefore, in the current stage of constructing "Mass Vernacular Literature," we still have to deal with this "leftover article from the May Fourth Movement" (which will be discussed later), and we must confront it with a fighting spirit, giving it a final, fatal blow to ensure its early demise. Moreover, this "Classical Chinese Revival" movement is not just the ulterior motives of a few people; it follows the entire social trend of restoring the old.

As for the vernacular that arose from the "May Fourth Movement," it was a manifestation of the emerging bourgeoisie's demand for democratic politics. It has indeed accomplished a great mission in anti-feudalism, but due to the defects of their class, they could not go further and do it thoroughly. They only circled around whether it was "vernacular" or "not vernacular" in words, and did not dare to delve into the bottom of society and connect with the masses, thus leaving a way for the "feudal" revival. On the other hand, due to the intensified oppression of international imperialism after the war and other relations, they were further distanced from the masses and turned back to join hands and compromise with feudalism. In language and writing, they only replaced "zhi hu zhe ye yan" with "de na ne ma," a disguised form of stereotyped writing.

Today's "Trend" publishes an article by Mr. Wang Gang, believing that "constructing Mass Vernacular" is not against "Vernacular Language." If Mr. Wang's words are correct, then the articles of the Saturday school, Zhang Henshui's novels, and things that appear wearing masks of "style," "spirituality," and "quotation style" (borrowing Mr. Hu Yuzhi's words), aren't they all written in vernacular (mass vernacular?)? Why do we need to construct "Mass Vernacular Literature" again? Isn't promoting "Mass Vernacular Literature" meddling? Mr. Wang criticizes others for mechanically setting things up in opposition, but he himself says, "In this battle against the revival of the old and against Classical Chinese, there is absolutely no reason to oppose 'Vernacular Literature.' Everyone should not only construct Mass Vernacular, but also 'Vernacular Literature'." This is mechanically setting them up in opposition.

What exactly is "Mass Vernacular Literature"? Is "Mass Vernacular Literature" completely different from "Vernacular"? Naturally not. "Mass Vernacular Literature" does not fall from the sky or spring from the ground; it develops with the practice of the masses. This point has already been mentioned earlier. Therefore, "Mass Vernacular Literature" is not completely against "Vernacular"; it is a unified opposite to "Vernacular." In other words, "Mass Vernacular Literature" is a higher level of "Vernacular," developing a certain part of "Vernacular" and discarding another part; it is the negation of "Vernacular."

From the above, we have briefly pointed out the differences and similarities between "Classical Chinese," "Vernacular," and "Mass Vernacular Literature," as well as why it is necessary to construct "Mass Vernacular Literature." As for further pointing out what constitutes "Mass Vernacular Literature," we will discuss it next time. At the same time, we want the masses to discuss it together; "Mass Vernacular Literature" belongs to the masses!

Sundries 265

— Long

The year before last, there was a great harvest, and rice prices plummeted. Farmers could not sell rice at a reasonable price and had almost no way to survive. Currently, rice prices are soaring, and famine is already a reality. Farmers not only have no rice to sell, but also have to buy expensive rice to eat. It's like a hunchback falling down, unable to land on either end, truly a dead end.

Without money, one naturally has no means to study abroad. With money, some people send them abroad. The other day, I saw ten little brothers and sisters being sent abroad, which was very enviable. But checking their background, most of them have influential connections. It can be seen that studying is indeed for those with power. Poor scholars shouldn't even think about it.

Yesterday, the Ping-Shen train started running. Suddenly, a violent bomb exploded on the train, resulting in one death, nineteen seriously injured, and over thirty slightly injured. I think these passengers were mostly very important, and they wanted to enjoy priority rights as soon as the train opened, desperately going to the Northeast, so they suffered this loss. It's truly a bitter experience they can't complain about.

The five Buddhist organizations in this city initiated the installation of a giant bell, weighing 30,000 kilograms, on the highest peak of Jiuhua Mountain in Anhui. It is said that the sound of this bell can be heard for hundreds of miles, which can save the souls of the hell realm. In this way, although people cannot get a way to live, ghosts have a way to live. What a great bell to save the souls!

— Yi Tong

Virtuous women who adhere to morality are easily deserted by their husbands. Unrestrained women who cater to new trends are instead sought after by the public.

Reminiscences of the Past Heat 267

— Yu

This unprecedented heat in the past decade has lasted for a week already, and judging from the situation, it is not expected to drop below 100 degrees within a few days. The epidemic hospital is already full, and people dying suddenly on the road are everywhere. This terrifying record seems to make the people of Shanghai uneasy, because everyone cannot find a way to avoid this unfortunate event. In this metropolis of three million people, the bourgeoisie is, after all, a minority among minorities. They can go to Mogan Mountain or Putuo Mountain to escape the summer heat. Even if they live in tall Western-style houses in Shanghai, there are summer resorts such as ice baths and night gardens for them to relax. Apart from them, the middle and lower classes, whether mentally or physically, cannot stop working because the mercury rises above 100 degrees. The diet and living habits of these people are often easily invaded by the demon of the epidemic. Therefore, it can be said with certainty that the majority of those who die from the epidemic are from the working class. As for the noble people, no matter how many weeks the unprecedented heat in the past sixty years persists, it has nothing to do with them.

We writers who make a living by selling manuscripts, sweating while writing manuscripts in this hot weather, although ten thousand times better than rickshaw pullers and coolies running under the scorching sun, the distance between mental labor and physical labor is only fifty steps or a hundred steps. However, compared to the farmers who look forward to the stars every night, we should be content. Although there have been two consecutive years of great harvests, due to the manipulation of rice prices and the oppression of land rent, the farmers are actually worse off than usual. The price of grain is so low that it is not enough for them to cover the cost of planting. Their hard work throughout the year has resulted in many debts. However, under heavy pressure, they still hope that grain prices will soar after this year's great harvest, pay off their debts, and live a happy year? Even if everything meets their expectations, it cannot compensate for their hardships! In the past week's unusual heat, how disappointed are the farmers! The source of their lives, the rice seedlings, are just tender shoots emerging from the water. How can they withstand a few days of extreme heat? From morning to night, they tirelessly use their legs to draw water, and the blisters on their feet are so painful that they cannot walk, but they have to draw water. As for the cattle, these are the farmers' most precious property. They are unwilling to let them do too much work; and in two years of crop failure, they reluctantly sold their most precious property to pay off their debts. Now that another year of famine is in sight, what is the pain of the farmers?

A Record of the Public Performance of Mellon Middle School 268

— Danfeng

The weather is so hot and stuffy that people cannot breathe freely, and everyone longs for the arrival of a rainstorm. The artists invited by Mellon Middle School came to a large-scale public performance in this enthusiastic and depressed mood.

Naturally, this performance deeply won the warm sympathy of the audience, which can be fully proved from the recent reactions in various newspapers. Indeed, the Chinese drama movement, starting with "Coal Miners" or "All Quiet on the Western Front" in 1930, has gone through "Roar, China!" until this year's "Noble People," "The Rising Moon," "Roar," "Jinbao," and finally this time's "Alarm" and "Storm on the Yangtze River," "Nora After Leaving." Whether in the content of the script or the form of the performance, obvious traces of progress can be seen. Although we admit that none of them can achieve 100% success, the proportion of success over failure is better than the latter.

This performance consists of four plays. Except for "Traveling Merchants in the Snow," which I never saw, I have seen the other three plays more than twice. Every audience member left a strong impression, and I have to write some messy opinions for the reference of those who participated in this performance. Where will Ibsen's Nora go after she leaves her family? This was a question that everyone paid attention to in the May Fourth era. Now, this question is answered in "Nora After Leaving." In this old society, in semi-colonial China, under the massacre of old etiquette, their only way out is to join the working masses and move towards a future of struggle. The presentation of this theme is naturally not distorted in principle. However, our playwright did not fully give the audience a strong sense of reality in terms of performance techniques. We always feel that the character played by Hu Ping, with her gorgeous clothes and affectionate husband, probably would not divorce her husband because of his passive surrender. Otherwise, it is described too inadequately. Suppose the author wrote about the destruction of her love, and that the imperialist cannons destroyed her family's economy, or the author wrote her as a healthy woman engaged in social movements, then the effect that the author expected could be discounted less. Also, the old mother's process of poisoning her children and committing suicide is also written very suddenly. Moreover, I think if we make her kill her children to teach the audience to hate her, we must strengthen her stubborn personality and vicious conspiracy, so the effect may be greater, isn't it? How terrible and solemn it is for a mother to kill her children. There also seems to be a lot of redundant dialogue for the news reporters, at least regarding the retelling of the poisoning process.

Due to the many technical shortcomings in the script, it is not easy to please in the performance. Generally speaking, this three-act play is not successful, although individually speaking, actors such as Hu Ping, Gu Menghu, Zhao Dan, Wang Hongyi, and Zhu Mingxian have considerable achievements. I don't want to say much about this play, and I hope the author will revise the script well. The performance on the night of the 1st was more skilled than on the night of the 30th.

On the other hand, "Storm on the Yangtze River" and "Alarm" have been very successful, whether in terms of script or performance. First of all, the former undoubtedly started the Chinese opera activity and adopted new content and forms. Of course, we also feel that there are many things that deserve to be improved. For example, in one performance on the 30th, we felt that the first act was probably unnecessary. At least, many words in the first act could be said at the beginning of the second act. Sure enough, when the last performance was staged, there was no first act. It started with a song and continued until the curtain closed in a tragic song, which was very compact; tragic poems, rough-lined pictures. However, if possible, after the playwright's revision, the content of the first act can be pieced together in the second act, and the indoor scene of the first act can be omitted. At the same time, the sound effects should also be made more tense and complex. As for the simple and substantial content, it indicates that the working masses on the banks of the Yangtze River are struggling under the forces of imperialism. Their common path is only to refuse to transport military supplies to them; not to build foreign wheat warehouses for them, and to participate in direct struggles together, striving for victory in blood and bullets. Finally, we want to talk about "Alarm," which is themed with depicting floods.

There is no doubt that this is another very successful work. Who is the manufacturer of the flood? We are told very clearly here. The people donated a lot of surcharges for repairing the dikes, but where did the money go? The director of the Water Conservancy Bureau made a fortune from opium and took his concubine to the provincial capital, making a joke of the lives of millions of people under the dikes. So the people under the dikes realized, grabbed the dangerous items, and saved their own lives, only to save themselves. With such realistic material and such a correct theme, in the sound of wind, rain, thunder, gongs, and the shouts of the masses, the vast number of people under the dikes bravely and tragically fought against man-made disasters.

The above two plays have achieved great success, whether it is the director, scenery, lighting, and even the sound effects, all have achieved great success. Especially all the actors, under the appropriate control of the director, and under their efforts, can take care of each other, and everyone is successful in just the right amount. Nie Er's old man was so calm in "Storm on the Yangtze River." Wang Ying's bravery, Lulu's stubbornness, the little actor Hainan's cry, and the musical melody of every crowd, the actions were all just right. In Alarm, Yuan Muzhi's old man, Zheng Junli's awakened youth, Zhao Dan's young farmer, Zhu Mingxian's aunt, Wu Mei's peasant woman, even the little boy and Hainan's siblings (especially Hainan covering his ears when he heard the thunder), everyone was working very hard and showing great talent. Fully expressing the truth is their great achievement, and the makeup of Yuan Muzhi and Nie Er is even more miraculous.

Well, in general, the full expression of the sense of reality in the above two plays should bear all the beautiful adjectives, which is determined by the content of the script and does not need to be explained. Finally, in addition to expressing our sincere respect for those who presided over and participated in this performance, we deeply believe that the Chinese drama movement is indeed bravely progressing in difficult and arduous situations.

The Scenery of Yu 269

A Man (Part 2) 270

— Dai Ni

He stood up, bothered her with the smoke from his cigarette, bent down and kissed her on the mouth, and sat on the edge of the bed. "Get up quickly and see the XX song and dance troupe. Those women don't wear pants," he gestured.

"Nothing good comes out of a dog's mouth!" She gave him a coquettish pat on the shoulder and jumped out of bed.

He retreated to the sofa, closed his eyes, almost wanting to fall asleep. The woman looked in the mirror and hurriedly put down her towel and sat on his body, shaking his head with both hands and saying, "What's making you unhappy? Tell me, tell me."

He pushed the woman away with force, "Wash your face!" The woman still wanted to twist onto him, but seeing his face was tense, she didn't push it, grumbling as she sat on the stool in front of the bed, combing and washing in front of the mirror.

"Hurry up!" he said anxiously.

The woman looked at the broken mirror next to the door and said with a pout, "What's the rush? It's not even two o'clock yet. You always make such a big noise when I invite you to the movies. If you don't want to go, fine. It's not like I sent you a red invitation!"

He made a gesture to stand up, but his whole body seemed to have no strength, so he ignored the woman's words and turned sideways to take out the cigarette case. There wasn't even one cigarette inside, so he threw it angrily on the table. "Do you have any cigarettes?"

"I wouldn't ask you for one if I had any."

"Go buy some!"

"Where's the money?" She turned around and held out her rouge-smeared hand.

He pulled out two five-yuan notes from his pocket and threw them over, but they fell halfway through the air. The woman picked them up and hid them in her vest pocket, then turned back to apply rouge to her cheeks.

"Go buy cigarettes!" he said impatiently, standing up. "It's not like I'll die from addiction! I haven't even eaten yet!" She looked up and made a face at him.

"Son of a bitch!" He grabbed her shoulder and pushed her, and the woman rolled straight onto the bed. He didn't even glance at her, opened the door and left.

Outside the alley, he changed two dimes at the cigarette shop, and after receiving the copper coins, he stood there in a daze, as if thinking about something. Finally, he put them in his pocket and jumped into a rickshaw on the side of the road. "Sir, where to?" the rickshaw puller asked, turning his head as he ran.

"Just pull!" He kicked the rickshaw puller's butt with his leather shoe.

He got off the rickshaw at the entrance of his alley. The Indian patrolman greeted him and asked, "Why not watch movie?" He shook his head and returned home.

"Where did you go?" his wife asked.

"Buying cigarettes." He reached into his pocket, but made no sound and didn't take anything out.

Amateur Mailbox

How to Relieve Her Worries 271

Dear Editor,

I have a very close friend. She has a gentle temperament and a quiet disposition, but it is not easy to hear her speak usually. She has a middle school education, has a strong desire to study, and especially likes to study art. She has some small artistic skills, but unfortunately, due to environmental and economic reasons, she finally dropped out of school halfway. She is now employed as a teacher at XX Elementary School. I admire her behavior and everything about her extremely; however, her eloquence is not good, and as for social interaction, it is of course very ordinary; therefore, she has few friends, and as for the opposite sex, she doesn't have a single one. Sir, I have told you about her movements and everything; now I want to trouble you to think of a way for her for the sake of my best friend!

In today's society where "men and women are equal and social interactions are open," she still adheres to extremely old etiquette. Although her colleagues admire and respect her, if someone occasionally mentions marriage to her, she will politely decline and say, "Marriage is a major matter that should be decided by parents." Since she is so conservative, shouldn't she follow "the words of a matchmaker and the orders of parents"? But she doesn't follow. This isn't right, that isn't right. It has been three or four years since she dropped out of school. In these few years, I know that she really doesn't have anyone else in mind; looking at her actions, it's as if she has embraced the idea of staying single.

Recently, I see that she is distracted, mentally tired, and her appearance is also haggard; so I have tried every means to ask her

Home
